Divine Decree
beginner
5 min
Divine Knowledge and Decree
The author quotes and explains the Tahawiyyah text on divine knowledge and decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's creation, decree, and provisions are all based on His eternal knowledge and will, and that His decree encompasses all things.

Core Idea
Allah's knowledge and will determine every aspect of creation, decree, and provision.

This lesson presents the foundational Islamic belief in divine decree (qadr) as articulated by Imam Tahawi. The text affirms that Allah created everything with His knowledge, set their destinies, and that nothing occurs except by His will. This understanding refutes misconceptions about human autonomy and establishes the framework for belief in qadr.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the repetition of key terms like 'عِلْمِهِ' and 'مَشِيئَتِهِ'.
2
Identify core statements
The passage makes several interrelated statements about Allah's knowledge, decree, and will. List them mentally: creation with knowledge, decree of destinies, appointment of terms, knowledge of deeds, command and prohibition, everything by His power and will.
3
Understand the commentary
The commentary expands each phrase: creation at the attachment of His will, decrees of good and evil, terms for provision and lifespan. It emphasizes that no one eats another's provision or dies before their term.
This commentary clarifies the practical implications of qadr.
4
Reflect on human will
The passage states that there is no will for the servants except what Allah wills. This is a key point in understanding the relationship between divine will and human free will in Sunni Islam.
This refutes the idea of absolute human free will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صفة العلم والإيمان بالقدر خَلَقَ الخَلْقَ بِعِلْمِهِ وَقَدَّرَ لَهُمْ أَقْدَارًا وَضَرَبَ لَهُمْ آجَالًا، لَمْ تَخْفَ عَلَيْهِ شَيْءٌ مِنْ أَفْعَالِهِمْ قَبْلَ أَنْ خَلَقَهُمْ وَعَلِمَ مَا هُمْ عَامِلُونَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَخْلُقَهُمْ، وَأَمَرَهُمْ بِطَاعَتِهِ وَنَهَاهُمْ عَنْ مَعْصِيَتِهِ. وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ يَجْرِي بِقُدْرَتِهِ وَمَشِيئَتِهِ، وَمَشِيئَتُهُ تَنْفُذُ وَلَا مَشِيئَةَ لِلْعِبَادِ إِلَّا مَا شَاءَ لَهُمْ؛ فَمَا شَاءَ لَهُمْ كَانَ وَمَا لَمْ يَشَأْ لَمْ يَكُنْ. خلق الخلق) بقدرته عند تعلق إرادته حسبما تعلق بعلمه) في سابقته (و) كذلك قدر لهم أقدارًا) من خير أو شر، وضرب لهم آجالا) لاستيفاء ما لهم من رزق وعمر؛ فلا يأكل أحد رزق غيره ولا يموت إلا بأجله وسببه. وفي هذا رد على المعتزلة القائلين: إن الحرام ليس رزقا والمقتول منقوص من أجله بناء على أصلهم الفاسد، وقد قال تعالى: (وَمَا مِن دَابَّةٍ فِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَّا عَلَى اللَّهِ رِزْقُهَا) [سورة هود: 6]، وقد عُرف في الخلق من لم يأكل غير الحرام قط فلو لم يكن الحرام رزقا لزم الخلف في الآية، وقال تعالى: (فَإِذَا جَاءَ أَجَلُهُمْ لَا يَسْتَأْخِرُونَ سَاعَةً وَلَا يَسْتَقْدِمُونَ) [سورة الأعراف: 34]، (إِنَّ أَجَلَ اللَّهِ إِذَا جَاءَ لَا يُؤَخِّرُ لَوْ كُنتُمْ تَعْلَمُونَ) [سورة نوح: 4] مع أن القتل فعل القاتل قائم به والموت قائم بالميت يخلقه الله تعالى عقب فعل الفاعل. كذا ذكر المثلى إلياس (١). لم يخف عليه شيء من أفعالهم) من قبل أن خلقهم)؛ بل وعلم ما هم عاملون) من (قبل أن يخلقهم).
The attribute of knowledge and belief in qadr: He created the creation with His knowledge and decreed for them decrees and appointed for them terms; nothing of their deeds was hidden from Him before He created them, and He knew what they would do before He created them, and He commanded them to obey Him and forbade them from disobeying Him. And everything proceeds by His power and will, and His will is executed, and there is no will for the servants except what He wills for them; so what He wills for them comes to be, and what He does not will does not come to be. (He created the creation) by His power when His will was attached according to what was attached to His knowledge in His precedence, and (likewise He decreed for them decrees) of good or evil, and (appointed for them terms) to receive their provision and lifespan; so no one eats the provision of another, nor does anyone die except by his appointed term and its cause. And in this is a refutation of the Mu'tazila who say: indeed the forbidden is not provision and the killed person is diminished from his term, based on their corrupt principle. And the Most High said: (And there is no creature on earth but that upon Allah is its provision) [Hud: 6], and it is known among creation that there are those who never ate anything but the forbidden; so if the forbidden were not provision, contradiction would follow in the verse. And the Most High said: (And when their term comes, they will not delay an hour nor advance it) [al-A'raf: 34], (Indeed, when the term of Allah comes, it will not be delayed, if you only knew) [Nuh: 4], despite the fact that killing is an act of the killer that inheres in him, and death inheres in the deceased, which Allah the Most High creates consequent to the agent's action. Thus mentioned al-Muthli Ilyas (1). (Nothing of their deeds was hidden from Him) before He created them; rather He knew what they would do before He created them).
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Tahawiyyah text regarding divine knowledge and belief in qadr (decree). It begins by quoting the matn: Allah created the creation with His knowledge, decreed their destinies and terms, knowing their deeds before creation, commanding obedience and forbidding sin. Everything runs by His power and will; His will is effective and no one wills except what He wills. Then the commentary explains each phrase: He created them at the attachment of His will according to His prior knowledge; He decreed their destinies of good and evil; He set terms for their provision and lifespan—so no one eats another's provision or dies before their time. This refutes the Mu'tazila who claim the forbidden is not rizq (provision) and that the killed person has a shortened term. The refutation uses two verses: one states that every creature's provision is from Allah, so if the forbidden were not provision, the verse would be false for those who eat only the forbidden; the other states that terms do not change. The commentary also clarifies that the act of killing belongs to the killer, while death is a separate creation by Allah at that moment. The passage ends by confirming that Allah knows deeds before creation.

Key Terms
قدر
مشيئة
رزق
أجل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Humans have complete free will independent of Allah's decree.
Correction: Allah's will is paramount; human will only operates within what Allah wills, as stated: 'there is no will for the servants except what He wills for them'.

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about human will?
A) Human will is independent of Allah's will.
B) Human will exists only as Allah wills.
C) Human will does not exist at all.
D) Human will is equal to Allah's will.

Key Takeaway
Allah's knowledge and will are the foundation of all creation, decree, and provision; nothing occurs outside His will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every moment of your life—including your failures and sins—occurs only because Allah willed it? How does that shape the way you seek forgiveness?
?
If Allah already knows every choice you will make, why do you still struggle with feeling that your actions are truly your own? Are you willing to surrender that illusion of independence today?
?
When something you desperately wanted does not happen, do you accept it as part of Allah's decree with contentment, or do you secretly resent it? How can you train your heart to embrace His will over yours?

Divine Decree
intermediate
5 min
Refuting the Mu'tazila on Provision and Lifespan
The author refutes Mu'tazila on rizq and ajal with Quranic evidence and rational arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic refutation of the Mu'tazila claims that the forbidden is not provision and that a killed person's lifespan is shortened.

Core Idea
The forbidden is still provision from Allah, and no term is shortened or extended—all is by Allah's decree.

In this passage, the commentator refutes two specific Mu'tazila doctrines: that the forbidden (haram) is not rizq (provision), and that a murdered person dies before their full term. Using Quranic evidence and logical reasoning, the author demonstrates that these claims contradict Allah's promises and the observed reality of some people eating only the forbidden.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the aggressive tone of refutation.
The passage begins with 'وفي هذا رد' signaling a direct refutation.
2
Identify the two Mu'tazila claims
The Mu'tazila claim that the forbidden is not provision, and that a killed person's term is shortened. Find these in the text.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
The author cites two verses: one on universal provision (Hud 6) and one on fixed terms (al-A'raf 34 and Nuh 4). Understand how each verse refutes the respective claim.
The logical argument for rizq: if the forbidden were not provision, the verse would be false for those who eat only the forbidden.
4
Understand the distinction between act and creation
The author clarifies that killing is the act of the killer, but death is created by Allah at that moment. This preserves the doctrine of fixed terms while maintaining human accountability.
This distinguishes between human action and divine creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صفة العلم والإيمان بالقدر خَلَقَ الخَلْقَ بِعِلْمِهِ وَقَدَّرَ لَهُمْ أَقْدَارًا وَضَرَبَ لَهُمْ آجَالًا، لَمْ تَخْفَ عَلَيْهِ شَيْءٌ مِنْ أَفْعَالِهِمْ قَبْلَ أَنْ خَلَقَهُمْ وَعَلِمَ مَا هُمْ عَامِلُونَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَخْلُقَهُمْ، وَأَمَرَهُمْ بِطَاعَتِهِ وَنَهَاهُمْ عَنْ مَعْصِيَتِهِ. وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ يَجْرِي بِقُدْرَتِهِ وَمَشِيئَتِهِ، وَمَشِيئَتُهُ تَنْفُذُ وَلَا مَشِيئَةَ لِلْعِبَادِ إِلَّا مَا شَاءَ لَهُمْ؛ فَمَا شَاءَ لَهُمْ كَانَ وَمَا لَمْ يَشَأْ لَمْ يَكُنْ. خلق الخلق) بقدرته عند تعلق إرادته حسبما تعلق بعلمه) في سابقته (و) كذلك قدر لهم أقدارًا) من خير أو شر، وضرب لهم آجالا) لاستيفاء ما لهم من رزق وعمر؛ فلا يأكل أحد رزق غيره ولا يموت إلا بأجله وسببه. وفي هذا رد على المعتزلة القائلين: إن الحرام ليس رزقا والمقتول منقوص من أجله بناء على أصلهم الفاسد، وقد قال تعالى: (وَمَا مِن دَابَّةٍ فِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَّا عَلَى اللَّهِ رِزْقُهَا) [سورة هود: 6]، وقد عُرف في الخلق من لم يأكل غير الحرام قط فلو لم يكن الحرام رزقا لزم الخلف في الآية، وقال تعالى: (فَإِذَا جَاءَ أَجَلُهُمْ لَا يَسْتَأْخِرُونَ سَاعَةً وَلَا يَسْتَقْدِمُونَ) [سورة الأعراف: 34]، (إِنَّ أَجَلَ اللَّهِ إِذَا جَاءَ لَا يُؤَخِّرُ لَوْ كُنتُمْ تَعْلَمُونَ) [سورة نوح: 4] مع أن القتل فعل القاتل قائم به والموت قائم بالميت يخلقه الله تعالى عقب فعل الفاعل. كذا ذكر المثلى إلياس (١). لم يخف عليه شيء من أفعالهم) من قبل أن خلقهم)؛ بل وعلم ما هم عاملون) من (قبل أن يخلقهم).
The attribute of knowledge and belief in qadr: He created the creation with His knowledge and decreed for them decrees and appointed for them terms; nothing of their deeds was hidden from Him before He created them, and He knew what they would do before He created them, and He commanded them to obey Him and forbade them from disobeying Him. And everything proceeds by His power and will, and His will is executed, and there is no will for the servants except what He wills for them; so what He wills for them comes to be, and what He does not will does not come to be. Key Terms
حرام
رزق
أجل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The forbidden (haram) is not provision from Allah, and a killed person dies before his appointed term.
Correction: The Quran confirms that all creatures receive provision from Allah, including the forbidden, and terms are fixed; killing does not shorten the term because death is created by Allah at that moment.

Checkpoint
What verse is used to refute the claim that the forbidden is not provision?
A) Al-A'raf 34
B) Hud 6
C) Nuh 4
D) Al-Baqara 30

Key Takeaway
The forbidden is still provision from Allah, and no term is shortened or extended; all is by Allah's decree.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you have ever consumed anything forbidden—whether in food, drink, or wealth—did you truly believe that Allah still provided it to you? Or did you think, like the Mu'tazila, that it had no connection to Allah's provision? How does this verse (Hud 6) change your view of what you consume tomorrow?
?
When you fear death or worry about losing a loved one to an accident or murder, do you secretly think that their term was cut short? This lesson teaches that no term is shortened. How does that transform your grief—or your fear—into trust in Allah's decree?
?
The Mu'tazila denied that the forbidden is provision because they could not reconcile evil means with divine provision. Are there areas in your life where you deny Allah's hand because the circumstances seem evil or unjust? Will you repent of that hidden doubt and accept that Allah's provision encompasses all?

Divine Decree
beginner
4 min
All Events Occur by Allah's Power and Will
The commentator affirms total divine control over all events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that every event in the universe, including human actions, occurs solely by Allah's power and will, as affirmed by Quranic verses.

Core Idea
Everything happens by Allah's power and will; nothing is outside His control.

This lesson establishes the foundational belief that every event in the cosmos is under Allah's absolute power and will. The commentator presents Quranic evidence to affirm that creation and determination are entirely from Allah, leaving no room for independent agency.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses
Read the three verses cited by the commentator. Notice how each verse emphasizes Allah's exclusive role in creation and determination.
The verses are from Surah Ar-Ra'd, Al-Furqan, and As-Saffat.
2
Understand the scope of divine power
The commentator states that everything in the universe occurs by Allah's power and will. Reflect on what 'everything' includes – from natural events to human actions.
3
Connect to the commentary's statement
The opening sentence is a comprehensive claim. See how the three verses serve as proof that nothing occurs independently of Allah's power and will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل شيء يجري في الكون إنما هو بقدرته ومشيئته كما قال تعالى: {خَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ} [سورة الرعد: 16]، {وَخَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَقَدَّرَهُ تَقْدِيرًا} [سورة الفرقان: 2]، {وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ} [سورة الصافات: 96]. ومشيئته تنفذ حكم ما شاء وأراد، ولا مشيئة للعباد إلا حيث وافقت ما شاء الله لهم وأراد؛ فما شاء لهم كان أي وجد، وما لم يشأ لهم لم يكن لم يوجد أي ما تعلقت المشيئة وهي الإرادة الإلهية – بوجوده يوجد؛ لتعلق العلم بوجوده، وما لم تتعلق المشيئة بوجوده لا يوجد؛ لتعلق العلم بعدم وجوده، وفي هذا رد على المعتزلة القائلين: إنما يريد الله من أفعال العباد ما كان طاعة والمعاصي والقبائح واقعة بإرادة العبد على خلاف إرادة الله تعالى، وقد قال تعالى: {وَمَا تَشَاءُونَ إِلَّا أَن يَشَاءَ اللَّهُ} [سورة الإنسان: 30]، وهم قد شاءوا المعاصي فكانت بمشيئة الله تعالى بهذا النص.
And everything that occurs in the universe is only by His power and His will, as Allah said: 'He created everything' [13:16], 'and He created everything and determined it with precise determination' [25:2], 'and Allah created you and what you do' [37:96]. And His will executes the decree of what He wills and intends, and there is no will for the servants except where it coincides with what Allah wills and intends for them; so what He wills for them is, i.e., exists, and what He does not will for them is not, does not exist; i.e., whatever the will, which is the divine intention, attaches to its existence exists, due to the attachment of knowledge to its existence, and whatever the will does not attach to its existence does not exist, due to the attachment of knowledge to its non-existence. And in this is a refutation of the Mu'tazila who say: Allah only wills from the actions of the servants what is obedience, and sins and evil deeds occur by the will of the servant contrary to the will of Allah. And Allah said: 'But you do not will except that Allah wills' [76:30], and they have willed sins, so they occurred by the will of Allah according to this text.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage proves that all events in the universe occur by Allah's power and will, citing three Quranic verses. The commentator explains that human will is entirely dependent on Allah's will; whatever Allah wills exists, and whatever He does not will does not exist. The relationship between divine will and knowledge is clarified: existence or non-existence is determined by the attachment of will, which is based on knowledge. Then a refutation of the Mu'tazila is given: they claim that Allah wills only obedience, while sins occur by the servant's will contrary to Allah's will. The commentator counter-cites the verse 'But you do not will except that Allah wills' (76:30), arguing that since the servants will sins, and this verse states that their will is contingent on Allah's will, sins must also be by Allah's will.

Key Terms
قدرة (power)
مشيئة (will)
خلق (creation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that events occur through a combination of Allah's will and independent causes.
Correction: The passage affirms that everything is solely by His power and will; no event occurs independently of His control.

Checkpoint
Which verse is cited to show that Allah creates human actions?
A) 'He created everything' (13:16)
B) 'And Allah created you and what you do' (37:96)
C) 'And He created everything and determined it with precise determination' (25:2)
D) 'But you do not will except that Allah wills' (76:30)

Key Takeaway
Everything in the universe, including human actions, occurs by Allah's power and will, as proven by clear Quranic verses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every good and bad event in your life is by Allah's power and will? When something goes wrong, do you complain or submit to His decree? What would change in your attitude if you lived this reality every moment?
?
The verse says Allah created your actions. How does that change your view of your own deeds? Are you proud of your good deeds as if you did them alone, or do you recognize that Allah is the creator of your obedience?
?
If your every action is created by Allah, what does that mean for your need for His help? How often do you pray 'Guide us to the straight path' with real awareness that He controls your actions? Will you commit to praying with that understanding starting today?

Divine Decree
intermediate
5 min
Human Will Depends on Divine Will and Refutation of Mu'tazila
Commentary on human will dependency and refutation of Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that human will is entirely dependent on Allah's will, and how this refutes the Mu'tazila claim that sins occur against Allah's will.

Core Idea
Human will is utterly dependent on Allah's will; nothing can be willed without His permission.

The commentator now addresses the nature of human will and its relation to divine will. He clarifies that servants have no will except what Allah wills for them, and then refutes the Mu'tazila who claim that sins occur by the servant's will contrary to Allah's will. The key proof text is the Quranic verse 'But you do not will except that Allah wills.'

Guided Path
1
Grasp the dependency of human will
The commentator states there is no will for servants except what coincides with Allah's will. Understand this as a complete subordination of human will to divine will.
This is a core Sunni belief.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila position
The Mu'tazila argued that Allah wills only obedience, while sins are willed solely by the servant. Notice how this contradicts the commentator's claim.
3
Analyze the refutation verse
The commentator quotes 'But you do not will except that Allah wills' (76:30). Think: if sinners will sins, and this verse conditions their will on Allah's will, then sins must be by Allah's will as well.
This is a powerful logical argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل شيء يجري في الكون إنما هو بقدرته ومشيئته كما قال تعالى: {خَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ} [سورة الرعد: 16]، {وَخَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَقَدَّرَهُ تَقْدِيرًا} [سورة الفرقان: 2]، {وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ} [سورة الصافات: 96]. ومشيئته تنفذ حكم ما شاء وأراد، ولا مشيئة للعباد إلا حيث وافقت ما شاء الله لهم وأراد؛ فما شاء لهم كان أي وجد، وما لم يشأ لهم لم يكن لم يوجد أي ما تعلقت المشيئة وهي الإرادة الإلهية – بوجوده يوجد؛ لتعلق العلم بوجوده، وما لم تتعلق المشيئة بوجوده لا يوجد؛ لتعلق العلم بعدم وجوده، وفي هذا رد على المعتزلة القائلين: إنما يريد الله من أفعال العباد ما كان طاعة والمعاصي والقبائح واقعة بإرادة العبد على خلاف إرادة الله تعالى، وقد قال تعالى: {وَمَا تَشَاءُونَ إِلَّا أَن يَشَاءَ اللَّهُ} [سورة الإنسان: 30]، وهم قد شاءوا المعاصي فكانت بمشيئة الله تعالى بهذا النص.
And everything that occurs in the universe is only by His power and His will, as Allah said: 'He created everything' [13:16], 'and He created everything and determined it with precise determination' [25:2], 'and Allah created you and what you do' [37:96]. And His will executes the decree of what He wills and intends, and there is no will for the servants except where it coincides with what Allah wills and intends for them; so what He wills for them is, i.e., exists, and what He does not will for them is not, does not exist; i.e., whatever the will, which is the divine intention, attaches to its existence exists, due to the attachment of knowledge to its existence, and whatever the will does not attach to its existence does not exist, due to the attachment of knowledge to its non-existence. And in this is a refutation of the Mu'tazila who say: Allah only wills from the actions of the servants what is obedience, and sins and evil deeds occur by the will of the servant contrary to the will of Allah. And Allah said: 'But you do not will except that Allah wills' [76:30], and they have willed sins, so they occurred by the will of Allah according to this text.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage proves that all events in the universe occur by Allah's power and will, citing three Quranic verses. The commentator explains that human will is entirely dependent on Allah's will; whatever Allah wills exists, and whatever He does not will does not exist. The relationship between divine will and knowledge is clarified: existence or non-existence is determined by the attachment of will, which is based on knowledge. Then a refutation of the Mu'tazila is given: they claim that Allah wills only obedience, while sins occur by the servant's will contrary to Allah's will. The commentator counter-cites the verse 'But you do not will except that Allah wills' (76:30), arguing that since the servants will sins, and this verse states that their will is contingent on Allah's will, sins must also be by Allah's will.

Key Terms
مشيئة (will)
إرادة (intention)
أفعال العباد (actions of servants)
رد (refutation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sins occur against Allah's will because He does not command or approve of them.
Correction: The passage clarifies that sins still occur by Allah's will, as nothing occurs outside His will; the verse proves that the servants' will is contingent on Allah's will, so sins they will are also by Allah's will.

Key Takeaway
Human will is entirely dependent on Allah's will; even sins occur by Allah's will, as proven by the Quranic verse 'But you do not will except that Allah wills'.

Everything Occurs by God's Power and Will
Author cites verses to prove all events occur by God's power and will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all events in the universe, including human actions, occur by God's power and will as affirmed by Quranic verses.

Core Idea
All events are under God's power and will.

This passage establishes a foundational belief of Ahl al-Sunna: that everything in the universe, including human actions, happens by the power and will of Allah. The author cites three Quranic verses to prove this principle, which is central to understanding divine predestination (qadar).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to grasp the author's assertion about divine power and will.
The passage begins with God's commands and then moves to the central statement.
2
Identify the three Quranic verses
Find the three verses quoted and notice how each emphasizes that Allah creates or determines everything.
The verses are from Surat al-Ra'd, al-Furqan, and al-Saffat.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider what these verses collectively prove about human actions: that even they are created by Allah's power.
This sets the stage for understanding the refutation of the Mu'tazila in the next lesson.

And (He) indeed (commanded them to obey Him and promised them His mercy for it, and forbade them from disobeying Him) and threatened them for violating it with His punishment. That is, whatever the will—which is the divine intention—is attached to its existence, exists because knowledge is attached to its existence, and whatever the will is not attached to its existence does not exist because knowledge is attached to its non-existence. Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a proof and refutation. It begins by affirming that God commanded obedience and promised reward, and forbade disobedience with threat of punishment. Then it asserts the central qadar principle: everything in the universe occurs only by God's power and will. Three Quranic verses are cited: (He created everything), (He created everything and determined it), and (Allah created you and what you do). These establish that all things, including human actions, are created by God. Next, it explains that God's will is executive: whatever He wills happens, and whatever He does not will does not happen. Human will is only effective when it coincides with God's will. It then links will to knowledge: God's will attaches to what He knows will exist, and does not attach to what He knows will not exist. The passage concludes with a direct refutation of the Mu'tazila, who claimed that only obedient actions are willed by God, while sins occur by human will against God's will. The verse (You do not will except that Allah wills) is quoted to show that even sins occur by God's will, because humans will them only if God wills them to will. This passage strongly affirms divine predestination (qadar) and rejects the Mu'tazili doctrine of human independent will.

The Refutation of the Mu'tazila on Divine Will
Author refutes Mu'tazila by affirming divine will encompasses all actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that human will is subordinate to divine will and that even sins occur by God's will, refuting the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Human will depends on God's will.

After establishing that all events occur by God's power, the author now explains the relationship between divine and human will. He asserts that human will only exists when it agrees with God's will, and refutes the Mu'tazila who claim that sins occur against God's will.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the second part of the source, focusing on the explanation of divine will and the refutation.
Notice the logical connection between will and knowledge.
2
Understand the relationship of wills
Identify the key statement: 'there is no will for the servants except where it agrees with what Allah willed.'
This shows human will is not independent.
3
Analyze the refutation of Mu'tazila
Read how the author quotes the verse 'And you do not will except that Allah wills' to counter the Mu'tazili claim.
The verse proves that even sins are willed by Allah because humans only will what Allah wills them to will.

Defining Divine Protection, Cure, Misguidance, Abandonment, and Affliction
Commentary defines five divine acts and categorizes them as grace or justice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise meanings of five divine acts: protection, cure, misguidance, abandonment, and affliction, and how they are categorized as grace or justice.

Core Idea
Divine acts are either grace (fadl) or justice (adl), each rooted in God's perfect attributes.

This passage from the Tahawiyyah commentary defines key divine acts mentioned in the creed. Each term describes a different aspect of God's interaction with His creation, and each is assigned to either grace or justice. Understanding these definitions helps us see that God's actions are always consistent with His mercy and wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the opening section listing the five verbs (يعصم, يعافي, يضل, يخذل, يبتلي) and their definitions. Notice the pattern: two are said to be grace, three are justice.
The verbs 'protect' and 'cure' are labeled grace; the others are justice.
2
Learn the definition of protection (عصمة)
Protection is a disposition that makes a person avoid sins even when able to commit them. It is a grace from God.
This is not coercion but a divinely granted virtue.
3
Understand the opposite acts
Misguidance, abandonment, and affliction are opposite of guidance, support, and well-being. They are acts of justice and punishment.
They are not arbitrary but based on wisdom.
4
Reflect on the balance
Note how the passage explicitly assigns 'fadlan' (grace) to the first two and 'adlan' (justice) to the last three. This shows that divine actions are always either gracious or just.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعصم) من يشاء عصمته، وهي ملكة تحمل صاحبها على اجتناب المعاصي مع التمكن منها. قاله السيد (۳). (ويعافي) أي يدفع عن من يشاء) عافيته، وهي دفاع الله تعالى عن العبد. (فضلا) منه ومنة، ويضل من يشاء) إضلاله، وهو ضد الرشاد، (ويخذل) - بضم الذال يترك نصرته وعونه ( ويبتلي) بالشر من يشاء خذلانه وابتلاءه (عدلا) منه ونقمة. قال العارف السيد عبدالله الحداد في حكمه: «الخلق مع الحق لا يخلو أحد منهم أن يكون في إحدى الدائرتين؛ إما في دائرة الرحمة أو في دائرة الحكمة؛ فمن كان اليوم في دائرة الرحمة كان غدًا في دائرة الفضل، ومن كان اليوم في دائرة الحكمة كان غدًا في دائرة العدل اهـ. قال شارحها: «وجل هذا المقام أن الله تعالى كان موصوفًا في الأزل بأوصاف الرحمة؛ كالجود والكرم والرأفة واللطف والإحسان، وموصوفا بصفات النقمة؛ كالقهر والإضلال والانتقام؛ فقسم خلقه بإرادته قسمين؛ فمنهم من قسم لهم أن يكونوا مظاهر أوصاف الرحمة في الأغلب وإن كانوا لا يخلون عن الحكمة والعدل، ومنهم من قسم لهم أن يكونوا مظاهر صفات النقمة المشتملة على الحكمة في الأغلب وإن كانوا لا يخلون عن الرحمة والفضل، ثم أخرجهم من العدم إلى فضاء الوجود فسهل لكل ما قسم له، ثم إذا أوردهم في مورد القيامة جعل أهل دائرة الرحمة بفضله في آلاء لا تحصى، وجعل أهل دائرة الحكمة بعدله في بلايا لا تقصى؛ فمن وفقه الله للخير فلا يحمدون إلا إياه ومن ابتلي بالضير فلا يلومن إلا نفسه.
And He protects whom He wills: His protection ('isma) is a disposition that bears its possessor to avoid sins while having the ability to commit them. This is from al-Sayyid. And He cures: i.e., He repels from whom He wills His cure, which is Allah's defense of His slave. It is a grace (fadlan) from Him and a favor. He leads astray whom He wills: His misguidance is the opposite of right guidance. He abandons - with damm on the dhal - He leaves His aid and support. He afflicts with evil whom He wills: His abandonment and affliction is justice (adlan) from Him and a punishment. Al-`Arif al-Sayyid `Abdullah al-Haddad said in his aphorisms: 'The creatures with respect to the Truth are not free from being in one of two circles: either the circle of mercy or the circle of wisdom. Whoever today is in the circle of mercy will tomorrow be in the circle of grace, and whoever today is in the circle of wisdom will tomorrow be in the circle of justice.' Its commentator said: 'Great is this station: Allah was described in pre-eternity with attributes of mercy like generosity, honor, compassion, kindness, and beneficence, and described with attributes of punishment like force, misguidance, and vengeance. He divided His creation by His will into two groups: some He decreed to be manifestations of the attributes of mercy in the majority, although they are not free from wisdom and justice, and some He decreed to be manifestations of the attributes of punishment that include wisdom in the majority, although they are not free from mercy and grace. Then He brought them from non-existence into the space of existence and facilitated for each what He had decreed. Then, when He brings them to the gathering place of the Resurrection, He places the people of the circle of mercy by His grace in countless blessings, and He places the people of the circle of wisdom by His justice in endless afflictions. So whoever Allah grants success to do good should praise none but Him, and whoever is tried with harm should blame none but himself.'
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This is a commentary passage that first defines the terms from the Tahawiyyah creed. 'And He protects (ويعصم)' means that God creates in the person a disposition (ملكة) that makes him avoid sins even when able to commit them – this is divine protection. 'And He cures (ويعافي)' means God repels harm from the person, which is God's defense of the slave. Both of these are designated as grace (فضلا) and favor (منة) from God. Then the opposite acts: 'He leads astray (ويضل)' which is the opposite of right guidance, 'He abandons (ويخذل)' meaning He withdraws His aid and support, and 'He afflicts (ويبتلي)' meaning He tests with evil. These are designated as justice (عدلا) and punishment (نقمة) from Him. The commentator then elaborates on this distinction by quoting a sufi master, al-Sayyid `Abdullah al-Haddad, who divides all of creation with respect to God into two circles: the circle of mercy and the circle of wisdom. Those in the circle of mercy today will receive grace tomorrow (in the afterlife), and those in the circle of wisdom today will receive justice tomorrow. The commentator explains that God is described with both merciful attributes and punitive attributes in pre-eternity. He divides His creation into two groups according to His will: one group predominantly manifests His merciful attributes, and the other predominantly manifests His punitive attributes. However, neither group is entirely devoid of the other aspect. God then brings them into existence and makes it easy for each to follow what is decreed for them. Finally, on the Day of Judgment, He rewards the merciful group with countless blessings by His grace, and punishes the wisdom group with endless afflictions by His justice. The moral: one who is guided should thank God, and one who is tested should blame only himself. This is a profound statement on divine decree and human responsibility.

The Two Circles: Mercy and Wisdom
Commentary explains the two circles of divine dealing and their pre-eternal basis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the circles of mercy and wisdom, how they relate to God's pre-eternal attributes, and the final outcomes for each group.

Core Idea
All creation falls into either the circle of mercy or the circle of wisdom, reflecting God's eternal attributes of grace and justice.

After defining the individual acts, the commentator expands on the broader framework. He quotes a sage who divides all people into two circles: mercy and wisdom. The commentary then explains that God decreed in pre-eternity which group would predominantly manifest His merciful attributes and which would manifest His attributes of justice. This lesson explores that profound structure.

Guided Path
1
Read the two-circles aphorism
Read the quote from al-Sayyid Abdullah al-Haddad: all creatures are either in the circle of mercy or the circle of wisdom. Those in mercy today receive grace tomorrow; those in wisdom today receive justice tomorrow.
Note the temporal reference: today (this world) and tomorrow (afterlife).
2
Understand the pre-eternal background
The commentator explains that God had both merciful and punitive attributes from eternity. He divided creation into two groups to manifest these attributes.
This does not mean God created some for punishment without reason; it is based on His wisdom.
3
See the final outcomes
On the Day of Judgment, the circle of mercy receives endless blessings by grace, and the circle of wisdom receives endless afflictions by justice. The passage ends with an admonition: those guided should thank God, those tested should blame themselves.
This emphasizes human responsibility despite divine decree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعصم) من يشاء عصمته، وهي ملكة تحمل صاحبها على اجتناب المعاصي مع التمكن منها. قاله السيد (۳). (ويعافي) أي يدفع عن من يشاء) عافيته، وهي دفاع الله تعالى عن العبد. (فضلا) منه ومنة، ويضل من يشاء) إضلاله، وهو ضد الرشاد، (ويخذل) - بضم الذال يترك نصرته وعونه ( ويبتلي) بالشر من يشاء خذلانه وابتلاءه (عدلا) منه ونقمة. قال العارف السيد عبدالله الحداد في حكمه: «الخلق مع الحق لا يخلو أحد منهم أن يكون في إحدى الدائرتين؛ إما في دائرة الرحمة أو في دائرة الحكمة؛ فمن كان اليوم في دائرة الرحمة كان غدًا في دائرة الفضل، ومن كان اليوم في دائرة الحكمة كان غدًا في دائرة العدل اهـ. قال شارحها: «وجل هذا المقام أن الله تعالى كان موصوفًا في الأزل بأوصاف الرحمة؛ كالجود والكرم والرأفة واللطف والإحسان، وموصوفا بصفات النقمة؛ كالقهر والإضلال والانتقام؛ فقسم خلقه بإرادته قسمين؛ فمنهم من قسم لهم أن يكونوا مظاهر أوصاف الرحمة في الأغلب وإن كانوا لا يخلون عن الحكمة والعدل، ومنهم من قسم لهم أن يكونوا مظاهر صفات النقمة المشتملة على الحكمة في الأغلب وإن كانوا لا يخلون عن الرحمة والفضل، ثم أخرجهم من العدم إلى فضاء الوجود فسهل لكل ما قسم له، ثم إذا أوردهم في مورد القيامة جعل أهل دائرة الرحمة بفضله في آلاء لا تحصى، وجعل أهل دائرة الحكمة بعدله في بلايا لا تقصى؛ فمن وفقه الله للخير فلا يحمدون إلا إياه ومن ابتلي بالضير فلا يلومن إلا نفسه.
And He protects whom He wills: His protection ('isma) is a disposition that bears its possessor to avoid sins while having the ability to commit them. This is from al-Sayyid. And He cures: i.e., He repels from whom He wills His cure, which is Allah's defense of His slave. It is a grace (fadlan) from Him and a favor. He leads astray whom He wills: His misguidance is the opposite of right guidance. He abandons - with damm on the dhal - He leaves His aid and support. He afflicts with evil whom He wills: His abandonment and affliction is justice (adlan) from Him and a punishment. Al-`Arif al-Sayyid `Abdullah al-Haddad said in his aphorisms: 'The creatures with respect to the Truth are not free from being in one of two circles: either the circle of mercy or the circle of wisdom. Whoever today is in the circle of mercy will tomorrow be in the circle of grace, and whoever today is in the circle of wisdom will tomorrow be in the circle of justice.' Its commentator said: 'Great is this station: Allah was described in pre-eternity with attributes of mercy like generosity, honor, compassion, kindness, and beneficence, and described with attributes of punishment like force, misguidance, and vengeance. He divided His creation by His will into two groups: some He decreed to be manifestations of the attributes of mercy in the majority, although they are not free from wisdom and justice, and some He decreed to be manifestations of the attributes of punishment that include wisdom in the majority, although they are not free from mercy and grace. Then He brought them from non-existence into the space of existence and facilitated for each what He had decreed. Then, when He brings them to the gathering place of the Resurrection, He places the people of the circle of mercy by His grace in countless blessings, and He places the people of the circle of wisdom by His justice in endless afflictions. So whoever Allah grants success to do good should praise none but Him, and whoever is tried with harm should blame none but himself.'
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This is a commentary passage that first defines the terms from the Tahawiyyah creed. 'And He protects (ويعصم)' means that God creates in the person a disposition (ملكة) that makes him avoid sins even when able to commit them – this is divine protection. 'And He cures (ويعافي)' means God repels harm from the person, which is God's defense of the slave. Both of these are designated as grace (فضلا) and favor (منة) from God. Then the opposite acts: 'He leads astray (ويضل)' which is the opposite of right guidance, 'He abandons (ويخذل)' meaning He withdraws His aid and support, and 'He afflicts (ويبتلي)' meaning He tests with evil. These are designated as justice (عدلا) and punishment (نقمة) from Him. The commentator then elaborates on this distinction by quoting a sufi master, al-Sayyid `Abdullah al-Haddad, who divides all of creation with respect to God into two circles: the circle of mercy and the circle of wisdom. Those in the circle of mercy today will receive grace tomorrow (in the afterlife), and those in the circle of wisdom today will receive justice tomorrow. The commentator explains that God is described with both merciful attributes and punitive attributes in pre-eternity. He divides His creation into two groups according to His will: one group predominantly manifests His merciful attributes, and the other predominantly manifests His punitive attributes. However, neither group is entirely devoid of the other aspect. God then brings them into existence and makes it easy for each to follow what is decreed for them. Finally, on the Day of Judgment, He rewards the merciful group with countless blessings by His grace, and punishes the wisdom group with endless afflictions by His justice. The moral: one who is guided should thank God, and one who is tested should blame only himself. This is a profound statement on divine decree and human responsibility.

دائرة الحكمة

Misconception: Some think that God's predestination means people have no free will and are forced into their fate.
Correction: The passage states that success comes from God but blame is on oneself; this affirms human responsibility.

Key Takeaway
God's pre-eternal attributes of mercy and justice are manifested in two circles of creation, leading to just outcomes in the afterlife.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which circle do you find yourself in today—mercy or wisdom? Look at your life: are the blessings you enjoy causing you to praise God alone, or do you feel entitled? Are the trials you face prompting you to blame yourself or to resent God? Own your answer before Him.
?
The passage says that the people of the mercy circle will receive grace, and the people of the wisdom circle will receive justice. If you truly believed that every trial you face is perfectly just and every blessing is purely grace, how would your daily attitude change? Exactly what would you stop complaining about and start thanking for?
?
You cannot change the circle God decreed for you, but you can change how you respond. The commentator says: those guided to good praise God, those tried with harm blame themselves. Belief in Divine Predestination from the Tahawiyyah
Affirmation of belief in all predestined good and evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Tahawiyyah's affirmation that all predestined events—good and evil—are from Allah's will and decree.

Core Idea
All predestined good and evil come from Allah's will and wisdom.

The Tahawiyyah creed is a foundational Sunni text. In this passage, it affirms belief in divine predestination in its entirety, including both good and evil. This lesson will examine the exact wording and its implications for Sunni theology.

Guided Path
1

The Covenant of Adam and His Descendants
The author affirms the reality of the covenant of Adam and his descendants, citing Quran and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reality of the primordial covenant taken from Adam and his descendants, as affirmed by the Quran and hadith, and how it relates to divine predestination and human action.

Core Idea
Our destiny is sealed by Allah's knowledge, yet we act according to His will.

The belief in the covenant (mīthāq) is a core tenet of Sunni creed. This lesson presents the scriptural evidence for the covenant taken from Adam's progeny, including the famous hadith that describes how Allah extracted two groups—one for Paradise and one for Hell. We will see how this doctrine is reconciled with human responsibility and action.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the structure: affirmation, Quranic verse, wisdom, hadith, and exegetical view.
The passage is dense; read slowly to grasp each element.
2
Identify the Quranic proof and wisdom
Focus on verse 7:172 and the explanation that the testimony was taken to prevent claims of ignorance on the Day of Resurrection.
3
Understand the hadith on extraction
The hadith describes two groups extracted from Adam's back: one for Paradise, one for Hell. Note the question about action and the Prophet's response.
This hadith is recorded by al-Tirmidhi and classed as hasan.
4
Reconcile predestination and action
The Prophet explains that Allah causes each person to act according to their final outcome. This aligns divine decree with human responsibility.
5
Reflect on the exegetical view
Consider the interpretation that the extraction happened in an instant, similar to the resurrection. This underscores the test of faith in the unseen.

And the covenant that Allah Almighty took from Adam, peace be upon him, and his descendants is true. We say: the covenant that Allah Almighty took from Adam, peace be upon him, and his descendants, and made them testify to it, is true, established by the Book, as Allah Almighty said: {And when your Lord took from the children of Adam, from their backs, their descendants, and made them testify against themselves, 'Am I not your Lord?' They said, 'Yes, we have testified.'} [Surat al-A'raf: 172]. Then He, glorified and exalted, explained the wisdom of the witness-taking by His saying: {Lest you say} i.e., lest they say on the Day of Resurrection: 'Indeed, we were unaware of this.' And in Ma'alim al-Tanzil by al-Baghawi: it was narrated from Muslim ibn Yasar al-Juhani that he was asked about this verse and said: I heard the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, asked about it, and he said: 'Indeed, Allah Almighty created Adam, then wiped his back with His right hand, and extracted from him a progeny and said: These are for Paradise, and they will act with the deeds of the people of Paradise. Then He wiped his back and extracted from him a progeny and said: I created these for the Fire, and they will act with the deeds of the people of the Fire.' A man said: 'Then what is the point of action, O Messenger of Allah?' The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Indeed, Allah, when He creates a servant for Paradise, He employs him with the deeds of the people of Paradise until he dies upon a deed from the deeds of the people of Paradise, and thus He admits him to Paradise. And when He creates a servant for the Fire, He employs him with the deeds of the people of the Fire until he dies upon a deed from the deeds of the people of the Fire, and thus He admits him to the Fire.' Abu 'Isa said: a hasan hadith. And in al-Talwih by al-Sa'd: a group of exegetes held that Allah Almighty extracted the descendants of Adam, some from others, according to how they will procreate until the Day of Resurrection, in the shortest time, like the death of all by the blowing of the Trumpet and the life of all by the second blowing; He formed them, made them speak, took their covenant, then returned them to the loins of Adam, then made us forget that state as a trial so that we might believe in the unseen.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal affirmation and evidence-based exposition of the covenant (mīthāq) that Allah took from Adam and his descendants. It begins by stating that this covenant is true (ḥaqq). The author then clarifies that this covenant is established by the Quran, specifically citing verse 172 of Surat al-A'raf, where Allah describes taking the covenant from the children of Adam and making them testify to His lordship. The wisdom behind this witness-taking is then explained from the same verse: it was so that people could not claim ignorance on the Day of Resurrection. Next, the author quotes a hadith from al-Baghawi's commentary, narrated by Muslim ibn Yasar al-Juhani, who was asked about this verse. The hadith describes how Allah created Adam, then extracted two groups from his back—one destined for Paradise and one for Hell—and declared their destiny. A companion then asked the Prophet about the purpose of human action if everything is predestined. The Prophet replied that Allah causes each person to act according to their ultimate outcome, so that death occurs on a deed consistent with their final abode. This hadith is authenticated by Abu 'Isa (al-Tirmidhi) as 'hasan'. Finally, the passage cites al-Talwih, summarizing the view of many exegetes that the extraction of descendants happened all at once in a momentary duration, analogous to the resurrection after the Trumpet blasts. Allah then formed them, spoke to them, took the covenant, returned them to Adam's loins, and made them forget that event as a test of faith in the unseen. The entire passage affirms the reality of the primordial covenant and reconciles divine predestination with human action.

Key Terms
الميثاق
الإشهاد
ذرية
الجنة والنار
العمل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Divine predestination negates the need for human effort.
Correction: The hadith clarifies that Allah creates actions consistent with the predetermined outcome; actions are the means by which the decree is actualized.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The covenant of Adam's descendants is a true event, establishing Allah's lordship and predestination, while human actions are the means by which His decree is realized.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The covenant was taken from you before you were born, yet you do not remember it. How does the fact that you were once a witness to Allah's lordship impact your faith today? Are you living in a way that reflects that forgotten testimony?
?
When you sin, do you ever blame your fate ('this is what Allah wrote for me')? How does the Prophet's response about action—that Allah makes a person act according to their destiny—challenge that excuse? What is one specific change in your actions you can make today to align with being 'employed for Paradise'?

Allah's Eternal Knowledge and Predestination
Al-Tahawi states Allah's eternal knowledge of Paradise and Hell numbers and predestination of actions, with commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Allah's eternal knowledge of the number of people in Paradise and Hell, and their actions, relates to predestination, facilitation, and the importance of one's final state.

Core Idea
Allah's eternal knowledge fixes the numbers, yet actions are facilitated according to destiny, and the ending determines worth.

This is a dense but deeply important passage from al-Tahawi's creed. It tackles one of the most delicate questions in Islamic theology: how divine knowledge and predestination relate to human deeds. Al-Tahawi gives us a clear statement, and Imam al-Maydani's commentary brings out the nuances around facilitation, endings, and the prior decree.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the words of al-Tahawi and his commentator resonate before analyzing.
Notice the precise phrasing: 'جملة واحدة لا يزاد ولا ينقص'.
2
Identify the key claims
List the main doctrinal points: eternal knowledge of exact numbers, knowledge of deeds, facilitation for one's created purpose, deeds judged by endings, and prior decree.
The commentator expands each point in the same order.
3
Reflect on the commentary
Focus on al-Maydani's explanation of 'كل ميسر لما خلق له' and the quote from al-Nasafi about the possibility of change before death. Consider how endings are determined by the prior decree.
This reconcilie the fixity of divine knowledge with human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَدْ عَلِمَ اللهُ تَعَالَى فِيمَا لَمْ يَزَلْ عَدَدَ مَنْ يَدْخُلُ الجَنَّةَ وَيَدْخُلُ النَّارَ جُمْلَةً وَاحِدَةً لَا يُزَادُ في ذَلِكَ العَدَدِ وَلَا يُنْقَصُ مِنْهُ، وَكَذَلِكَ أَفْعَالَهُمْ فِيمَا عَلِمَ مِنْهُمْ أَنَّهُمْ يَفْعَلُونَهُ، وَكُلٌّ مُيَسَّرٌ لِمَا خُلِقَ لَهُ. وَالأَعْمَالُ بِالخَوَاتِمِ، وَالسَّعِيدُ مَنْ سَعِدَ بِقَضَاءِ اللهِ تَعَالَى وَالشَّقِيُّ مَنْ شَقِيَ بِقَضَاءِ اللهِ تَعَالَى. (و) نَقُولُ: (قَدْ عَلِمَ اللهُ تَعَالَى فِيمَا لَمْ يَزَلْ) أَيْ فِي عِلْمِهِ الأَزَلِيِّ الَّذِي لَمْ يَزَلْ (عَلَيْهِ) عَدَدُ مَنْ يَدْخُلُ الجَنَّةَ بِفَضْلِهِ وَمَنْ يَدْخُلُ النَّارَ بِعَدْلِهِ جُمْلَةً وَاحِدَةً لَا يُزَادُ فِي ذَلِكَ العَدَدِ المَعْلُومِ وَلَا يُنْقَصُ مِنْهُ، وَكَذَلِكَ أَفْعَالَهُمْ فِيمَا عَلِمَ مِنْهُمْ أَنَّهُمْ يَفْعَلُونَهُ مِنْ خَيْرٍ أَوْ شَرٍّ وَنَفْعٍ أَوْ ضَرٍّ، وَكُلٌّ مُيَسَّرٌ لِمَا خُلِقَ لَهُ؛ فَأَهْلُ السَّعَادَةِ يُيَسَّرُونَ لِعَمَلِ أَهْلِ السَّعَادَةِ، وَأَهْلُ الشَّقَاوَةِ يُيَسَّرُونَ لِعَمَلِ أَهْلِ الشَّقَاوَةِ. (وَالأَعْمَالُ) إِنَّمَا تُعْتَبَرُ (بِالخَوَاتِمِ) وَإِنْ كَانَ قَبْلَهَا يُوصَفُ بِضِدِّهَا، قَالَ النَّسَفِيُّ فِي عَقَائِدِهِ: وَالسَّعِيدُ قَدْ يَشْقَى وَالشَّقِيُّ قَدْ يَسْعَدُ. اهـ. وَالخَوَاتِيمُ مَبْنِيَّةٌ عَلَى سَابِقَةِ القَضَاءِ كَمَا أَشَارَ إِلَيْهِ بِقَوْلِهِ: (وَالسَّعِيدُ مَنْ سَعِدَ بِقَضَاءِ اللهِ تَعَالَى وَقَدَرِهِ وَالشَّقِيُّ مَنْ شَقِيَ بِقَضَاءِ اللهِ تَعَالَى وَقَدَرِهِ السَّابِقِ عَلَى وُجُودِهِ).
And Allah the Exalted has eternally known the number of those who enter Paradise and those who enter Hell as one aggregate, neither increased nor decreased from that number; and likewise their deeds, in what He knew that they would do; and each is facilitated for what he was created for. And deeds are by their endings; and the fortunate is the one who is fortunate by the decree of Allah the Exalted, and the wretched is the one who is wretched by the decree of Allah the Exalted. (And) we say: (Allah the Exalted has known eternally) i.e., in His eternal knowledge which has always been (upon Him) the number of those who enter Paradise by His grace and those who enter Hell by His justice as one aggregate, neither increased nor decreased from that known number; and likewise their deeds, in what He knew that they would do, of good or evil, benefit or harm; and each is facilitated for what he was created for; so the people of happiness are facilitated for the work of the people of happiness, and the people of wretchedness are facilitated for the work of the people of wretchedness. (And deeds) are only considered (by their endings) even if before them one is described with the opposite; al-Nasafi said in his creed: 'The fortunate may become wretched and the wretched may become fortunate.' End. And endings are built upon the prior decree as he indicated by his saying: (And the fortunate is the one who is fortunate by the decree of Allah the Exalted and His predestination, and the wretched is the one who is wretched by the decree of Allah the Exalted and His predestination prior to his existence).
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage consists of a creedal statement from al-Tahawi and its commentary by Imam al-Maydani. The creed asserts that Allah's eternal knowledge encompasses the exact number of inhabitants of Paradise and Hell, unchangeably; likewise, He knows all their deeds before they occur. The phrase 'each is facilitated for what he was created for' indicates that Allah predisposes each person toward their ultimate destiny. The commentator explains the creed point by point: Allah's knowledge is eternal, the numbers are fixed, deeds are known, and facilitation corresponds to one's created nature. The statement 'deeds are by their endings' means that final judgment depends on the end of one's life, not intermediate states; al-Nasafi is quoted to caution that one's state can change before death. The commentator concludes that endings are determined by the prior decree of Allah, which is unalterable.

Key Terms
علم الله الأزلي
السعادة
الشقاء
الخواتيم
القضاء
القدر
التيسير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The belief that predestination removes human responsibility or that one's fate is completely fixed regardless of actions.
Correction: The passage affirms that actions are known and facilitated, but the individual's end is determined by their actual deeds and the ultimate state, as demonstrated by the possibility of change before death. However, that final state is already decreed.

Checkpoint

B) The people of happiness are facilitated for the work of the people of happiness, and the people of wretchedness are facilitated for the work of the people of wretchedness
C) Everyone chooses freely regardless of their created nature
D) Only the fortunate are facilitated, not the wretched

Key Takeaway
Allah's eternal knowledge and decree are unalterable, but deeds are facilitated according to one's created nature, and the outcome is based on one's final state, which is determined by Allah's prior decree.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The passage says 'each is facilitated for what he was created for.' Look at your own life: what facilitation do you see—do you find yourself drawn towards acts of obedience or sin? What does that say about your created purpose, and what will you do to align with the ending you desire?

The Foundation of Happiness and Misery on Exception in Faith
Maydani analyzes the foundation of happiness and misery on exception in faith and resolves the dispute as verbal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the issue of happiness and misery relates to the issue of exception in faith, and why the disagreement between the two groups is merely verbal.

Core Idea
The dispute on happiness and misery is about wording, not reality.

Maydani explains that the apparent disagreement about whether a person's final state can change is actually based on a deeper issue: whether one can make an exception (istithna') when declaring someone a believer or disbeliever. He shows that both groups agree on the essential point—that the final outcome is what matters—and the difference is only in how they express it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Maydani builds his argument.
2
Identify the two positions
The passage describes two groups: those who permit exception in faith and those who forbid it. Each group looks at a different aspect of the issue.
One looks at the final outcome, the other at current rulings.
3
Understand the resolution
Maydani explains that the disagreement is verbal (lafzi) not substantive (ma'nawi). Both sides agree that pre-eternal happiness or misery is fixed and will manifest.
The author of Tahawiyyah used a phrase acceptable to both.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن مبنى هذه المسألة وهي مسألة السعادة والشقاوة على مسألة الاستثناء في الإيمان؛ فمن قال بجوازه في الإيمان نظرًا إلى الخاتمة ذهب إلى عدم التبدل، ومن قال بعدم جوازه نظرًا إلى تسمية الشرع المؤمن مؤمنا وإجراء أحكام الإيمان عليه وإن كان مآله الكفر والكافر كافرًا وإجراء أحكام الكفر عليه وإن كان مآله -الإيمان ذهب إلى حصول التبديل؛ فكل من الفريقين ناظر إلى طرف والخلاف بينهما مرجعه اللفظ دون المعنى؛ ولهذا لم يذكر المصنف له مسألة الاستثناء في الإيمان ولا صرح بأن الشقي يصير سعيدا وبالعكس، وإنما أتى بعبارة أجمع عليها الفريقان وهي أن العبرة في الخاتمة وأن من له سعادة في الأزل أو شقاوة فلا تتبدل بل لابد أن تنفذ وتظهر على ذلك الشخص ؛ فإن كان لها أمر في الدنيا معيَّن لابد أن تكون فيه فإذا انقضى أمدها تبدلت بضدها، وإذا لم يكن لها أمد معيَّن بقيت إلى الآخرة، وهذا المقدار لا خلاف فيه لأحد.
Know that the foundation of this issue—the issue of happiness and misery—is based on the issue of exception (istithna') in faith. For whoever says it is permissible regarding faith, considering the final outcome, holds that there is no change. And whoever says it is not permissible, considering the Sharia's naming a believer as a believer and applying the rulings of faith upon him even if his end is disbelief, and a disbeliever as a disbeliever and applying the rulings of disbelief upon him even if his end is faith, holds that change occurs. Thus each of the two groups looks at one side, and the disagreement between them reduces to wording (lafz) not meaning (ma'na). For this reason, the author did not mention the issue of exception (istithna') in faith, nor did he state explicitly that the wretched becomes happy or vice versa. Rather, he came with a phrase that both groups agreed upon: that the consideration is in the final outcome, and that whoever has happiness in pre-eternity or misery does not change, but rather it must be executed and appear upon that person. If it has a specified term in this world, it must occur in it, and when its term expires, it changes to its opposite. And if it does not have a specified term, it remains until the Hereafter. And this amount is not disputed by anyone.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is an analysis by the commentator (Maydani) of the relationship between two issues: the issue of happiness and misery (al-sa'ada wa al-shaqawa) and the issue of exception (istithna') in faith. He states that the foundation of the issue of happiness and misery is built upon the issue of exception in faith. He then explains the two positions: those who permit exception in faith, looking to the final outcome (al-khatima), hold that there is no change (tabaddul) in a person's ultimate state. Those who forbid exception, looking to the current ruling of the Sharia that labels a person based on their present state (even if the end is different), hold that change does occur. He then clarifies that both groups are actually looking at different aspects, and the dispute is verbal (lafzi) rather than substantive (ma'nawi). This is why the author of the Tahawiyyah (Imam Tahawi) avoided delving into the exception issue and instead used a phrase acceptable to both: that the real consideration is the final outcome, and that pre-eternal happiness or misery is not subject to change; it must manifest itself. If it has a fixed term in this world, it will manifest during that term and then change to its opposite when the term ends. If it has no fixed term, it persists to the Hereafter. This much is agreed upon by all.

Key Terms
السعادة
الشقاوة
الاستثناء في الإيمان
التبدل
اللفظ
المعنى
الخاتمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the disagreement about change in happiness and misery is about actual change in God's decree.
Correction: It is actually only about how to interpret the rulings of faith and disbelief in this life, not about the reality of God's pre-eternal decree.

Checkpoint

A) The issue of qada and qadr

Key Takeaway
The disagreement about happiness and misery is a verbal dispute because both sides agree on the fundamental principle that the final outcome is decisive and pre-eternal states are fixed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The dispute is only about wording, not meaning. Are there areas of your own faith where you engage in verbal debates while ignoring the weightier matters of the heart and action? What would it look like to move from arguing about words to focusing on your actual relationship with Allah?

The Foundation of Qadar: Allah's Secret and the Prohibition of Delving into It
Definition of qadar, its secrecy, and warning against investigation, with refutation of Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that qadar is a secret of Allah, that investigating it leads to loss, and that the Qadariyya sect was refuted for denying or misattributing qadar.

Core Idea
Qadar is Allah's secret; pondering it is destruction, questioning it is disbelief.

This lesson from the Sharh Tahawiyyah establishes a core Sunni principle: qadar (divine decree) is a hidden secret known only to Allah. The passage issues a stern warning against delving into its mysteries, citing the Quranic verse 'He is not questioned about what He does'. It then defines qadar and refutes the Qadariyya sect.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Warning
Read the first part of the passage where the author declares that the foundation of qadar is a secret and that delving into it leads to abandonment, deprivation, and transgression.
Notice the strong language: 'dhari'at al-khidhlan, sullam al-hirman, darajat al-tughyan'.
2
Learn the Definition
Examine how 'asl al-qadr' is defined linguistically and technically as Allah's knowledge of what will be, and its expression as qada.
The definition includes both pre-measurement and actual bringing into existence.
3
Know the Refutation
Grasp the refutation of the Qadariyya sect: their denial of pre-measurement, their later belief that evil comes from other than Allah, and their attempted reversal of the label.
The author concludes by affirming that Sunnis attribute all matters to Allah, while Qadariyya attribute to themselves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَصْلُ القَدَرِ سِرُ اللَّهِ فِي خَلْقِهِ لَمْ يَطَّلِعُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ مَلَكٌ مُقَرَّبُ وَلَا نَبِيٌّ مُرْسَلٌ، وَالتَّعَمُّقُ وَالنَّظَرُ فِي ذَلِكَ ذَرِيعَةُ الخِذْلَانِ وَسُلَّمُ الحِرْمَانِ وَدَرَجَةُ الطُّغْيَانِ، فَاحْذَرَ كُلَّ الحَذَرِ مِنْ ذَلِكَ نَظَرًا أَوْ فِكْرًا أَوْ وَسْوَسَةً؛ فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى طَوَى عِلْمَ القَدَرِ عَنْ أَنَامِهِ وَنَهَاهُمْ عَنْ مَرَامِهِ كَمَا قَالَ فِي كِتَابِهِ: لَا يُسْتَلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ وَهُمْ يُسْطُونَ سورة الأنبياء آية: (۲۳)؛ فَمَنْ سَأَلَ: لِمَ فَعَلَ؟ فَقَدْ رَدَّ حُكْمَ كِتَابِ اللهِ، وَمَنْ رَدَّ حُكْمَ كِتَابِ اللهِ تَعَالَى كَانَ مِنَ الكَافِرِينَ. (وأصل (القدر) بتحريك الدال وتسكينها، مصدر قدرت الشيء بفتح الدال وتخفيفها إذا أحطت بمقداره أي حقيقته (سر الله تعالى أي علمه بما يكون (في خلقه ثم إيجاده ما سبق في علمه أنه يوجد، ويعبر عن هذا بقضائه. قال الإمام النووي في شرحه على صحيح الإمام مسلم: اعلم أن مذهب أهل السنة إثبات القدر، وهو أنه سبحانه وتعالى قدر الأشياء في القدم وعلم سبحانه وتعالى أنها ستقع في أوقات معلومة عنده تعالى وعلى صفات مخصوصة؛ فهي تقع على حسب ما قدرها سبحانه وتعالى، وأنكرت القدرية هذا وزعمت أنه سبحانه وتعالى لم يقدرها في سابق علمه وأنها مستأنفة العلم؛ أي يعلمها سبحانه وتعالى بعد وقوعها؛ تعالى ربنا عن أقوالهم الباطلة علوا كبيرًا، وسميت هذه الفرقة القدرية لإنكارهم القدر، وقد انقرضت هذه الفرقة، وصارت القدرية في هذا الزمان تعتقد أن الخير من الله والشر من غيره، تعالى الله عن ذلك، قال إمام الحرمين في إرشاده: «إن بعض القدرية قال: لسنا بقدرية بل أنتم القدرية لاعتقادكم إثبات القدر، وهذه جهالة وتواقح؛ فإننا بحمد الله تعالى نفوض أمورنا الله تعالى ونضيف جميع الأمور إليه، وهؤلاء الجهلة يضيفونها إلى أنفسهم، ومضيف الشيء إلى نفسه أولى بأن ينسب إليه ممن يعتقده لغيره، وقد
And the foundation of al-qadr (divine decree) is a secret of Allah concerning His creation; no angel brought near nor prophet sent has been informed of that. And delving deep and investigating into it is a means of abandonment, a ladder of deprivation, and a step of transgression. So beware with all caution of that, whether by looking, thinking, or whispering. For indeed Allah Almighty has folded up the knowledge of qadr from His creatures and forbade them from seeking it, as He said in His Book: 'He is not questioned about what He does, but they will be questioned' (Quran 21:23). So whoever asks: 'Why did He do?' has rejected the ruling of Allah's Book, and whoever rejects the ruling of Allah's Book becomes among the disbelievers. (And 'asl al-qadr' — with the dāl voweled or unvoweled, is the verbal noun of 'qadartu al-shay'' with the dāl opened and not geminated, when you comprehend its measure, i.e., its reality — is the secret of Allah Almighty, i.e., His knowledge of what will be in His creation, then bringing into existence what preceded in His knowledge that He would bring into existence, and this is expressed by His 'qada''. Imam al-Nawawi said in his commentary on Sahih Muslim: Know that the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunna is affirming al-qadr, and it is that He, exalted, measured things in pre-eternity and knew, exalted, that they would occur at known times with Him and in specific ways; so they occur according to what He measured. And the Qadariyya denied this and claimed that He, exalted, did not measure them in His prior knowledge and that they are 'initiated knowledge,' i.e., He knows them after their occurrence. Exalted is our Lord above their false statements, greatly. And this sect was called 'Qadariyya' because of their denial of qadr. This sect has become extinct, and the Qadariyya in this time believe that good is from Allah and evil from other than Him. Exalted is Allah above that. Imam al-Haramayn said in his 'Irshad': 'Some of the Qadariyya said: We are not Qadariyya, rather you are Qadariyya because of your belief in affirming qadr.' This is ignorance and impudence; for we, by the praise of Allah, delegate our affairs to Allah and attribute all matters to Him, while these ignorant ones attribute them to themselves. And the attributer of a thing to himself is more entitled to be ascribed to it than the one who believes it for another. And
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a definition and warning regarding the doctrine of qadar (divine decree). It begins by stating that the foundation of qadar is a secret of Allah concerning His creation, which no angel or prophet has been allowed to access. It then issues a strong warning: delving into qadar is a means of abandonment (khidhlan), a ladder of deprivation (hirman), and a step of transgression (tughyan). The author commands extreme caution against any form of investigation, contemplation, or whispering about it. The reason given is that Allah has hidden knowledge of qadar from His creatures and forbade them from seeking it, as indicated in the Quranic verse: "He is not questioned about what He does, but they will be questioned" (21:23). The author then explains that whoever asks 'Why did He do?' has rejected the ruling of Allah's Book, and such rejection constitutes disbelief. Next, he provides a linguistic and technical definition of qadar: it is a verbal noun from 'qadara' meaning to measure or estimate; in context, it refers to Allah's knowledge of what will be and His bringing it into existence accordingly, also called qada'. He then quotes Imam al-Nawawi, who explains the Sunni position: affirming qadr means that Allah measured all things in pre-eternity and foreknew them, and they occur as He measured. The Qadariyya sect denied this, claiming that Allah's knowledge is initiated (i.e., He only knows things after they occur). The author notes that this sect has become extinct, but a later form of Qadariyya holds that good is from Allah and evil from other than Him, which is also rejected. Finally, he quotes Imam al-Haramayn refuting an argument by some Qadariyya who try to reverse the label, saying the Sunnis are the real Qadariyya because they affirm qadar. The author dismisses this as ignorance and impudence, pointing out that the Sunnis attribute all matters to Allah, while the Qadariyya attribute things to themselves, so the term more appropriately applies to those who attribute things to themselves.

Key Terms

سر الله
التعمق
القدرية
القضاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that discussing qadar is permissible as long as one does not rebel or question Allah's actions.
Correction: The passage declares that even deep thought and investigation into qadar is a means of abandonment, a ladder of deprivation, and a step of transgression, and commands caution from any form of thinking or whispering about it.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on someone who asks 'Why did Allah do this?' regarding matters of qadar?
A) It is permissible if asked with sincere intent.

C) It is a minor sin but not disbelief.
D) It is recommended to ask for deeper understanding.

Key Takeaway
Qadar is a divine secret; investigating it leads to loss, and questioning Allah's actions is disbelief; Ahl al-Sunna affirm qadar while Qadariyya reject it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
You believe in qadar, but do you truly attribute all matters—good and evil—to Allah alone, or is there a subtle tendency in your heart to attribute evil to other sources? How can you train your heart to see everything as from Allah, as the Ahl al-Sunna do?

The Secret of Divine Decree
Maydani states that qadar is Allah's secret and warns against investigating it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the foundation of divine decree is a secret of Allah and that investigating it leads to spiritual harm.

Core Idea
Qadar is Allah's secret; delving into it leads to abandonment, deprivation, and tyranny.

Imam Maydani opens by establishing that the essence of divine decree (qadar) is a concealed secret of Allah, inaccessible even to angels and prophets. He then warns that any attempt to investigate it is a path to spiritual ruin. Let's read his exact words and unpack their meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation to get the gist.
Notice the three consequences listed.
2
Identify the three consequences
The passage lists three outcomes of delving into qadar: a means of abandonment, a ladder of deprivation, and a degree of tyranny. Ponder their escalating severity.
These are not just warnings but spiritual dangers.
3
Reflect on the command to avoid
The command 'faḥdhar kulla al-ḥadhar' emphasizes extreme caution, extending even to thoughts and whispers.
This shows the gravity of the issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَصْلُ الْقَدَرِ سِرُّ اللَّهِ فِي خَلْقِهِ لَمْ يَطَّلِعْ عَلَى ذَلِكَ مَلَكٌ مُقَرَّبٌ وَلَا نَبِيٌّ مُرْسَلٌ، وَالتَّعَمُّقُ وَالنَّظَرُ فِي ذَلِكَ ذَرِيعَةُ الْخِذْلَانِ وَسُلَّمُ الْحِرْمَانِ وَدَرَجَةُ الطُّغْيَانِ، فَاحْذَرْ كُلَّ الْحَذَرِ مِنْ ذَلِكَ نَظَرًا أَوْ فِكْرًا أَوْ وَسْوَسَةً؛ فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى طَوَى عِلْمَ الْقَدَرِ عَنْ أَنَامِهِ وَنَهَاهُمْ عَنْ مَرَامِهِ كَمَا قَالَ فِي كِتَابِهِ: لَا يُسْأَلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ وَهُمْ يُسْأَلُونَ سورة الأنبياء آية: (٢٣)؛ فَمَنْ سَأَلَ: لِمَ فَعَلَ؟ فَقَدْ رَدَّ حُكْمَ كِتَابِ اللهِ، وَمَنْ رَدَّ حُكْمَ كِتَابِ اللهِ تَعَالَى كَانَ مِنَ الْكَافِرِينَ.
The foundation of qadar (divine decree) is the secret of Allah in His creation, no angel brought near nor prophet sent has been informed of that. And delving deeply and investigating it is a means of abandonment, a ladder of deprivation, and a degree of tyranny. So be extremely cautious of that, whether by looking, thinking, or whispering. For Allah Most High has concealed the knowledge of qadar from His creatures and forbade them from seeking it, as He said in His Book: 'He is not asked about what He does, but they are asked' (Surat al-Anbiya', verse 23). So whoever asks: 'Why did He do?' has rejected the ruling of the Book of Allah, and whoever rejects the ruling of the Book of Allah Most High is among the disbelievers.

Commentary
This passage is a warning against delving into the nature of divine decree (qadar). The author begins by stating that the origin of qadar is a secret of Allah in His creation, meaning that no angel or prophet has been given access to its full reality. He then lists three consequences of investigating it: it is a means of abandonment (khidhlān), a ladder of deprivation (ḥirmān), and a degree of tyranny (ṭughyān). The reader is commanded to be extremely cautious of any thought, speculation, or whisper on this matter. The reason given is that Allah has concealed the knowledge of qadar from His creatures and prohibited them from seeking it, citing the Quranic verse: 'He is not asked about what He does, but they are asked' (21:23). The author then draws a severe conclusion: anyone who asks 'Why did He do?' has rejected the ruling of Allah's Book, and whoever rejects that ruling is among the disbelievers.

Maydani explains the reason for the prohibition and the ruling on questioning qadar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why questioning Allah's actions is prohibited and the severe consequence of doing so.

Core Idea
Asking 'Why?' about Allah's decree rejects the Quran and can lead to disbelief.

In the second part of this passage, Imam Maydani provides the scriptural basis for the prohibition: Allah has concealed the knowledge of qadar and forbade seeking it. He then cites a Quranic verse and draws a serious conclusion.

Guided Path

2
Understand the Quranic proof

This is the foundation of the prohibition.
3
Grasp the consequence of questioning
Whoever asks 'Why did He do?' has rejected the Quran's ruling, and that rejection amounts to disbelief.
This is a very severe outcome.
