Definition of Qadar and Ahl al-Sunna Belief
Maydani defines qadar and states the Ahl al-Sunna belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic and technical meaning of qadar and the Ahl al-Sunna belief in divine pre-determination.

Core Idea
Qadar is Allah's eternal knowledge and decree; all things occur as He predetermined.

This lesson opens with the definition of qadar, a central concept in Islamic theology. The author explains both the linguistic root and the technical meaning, then quotes Imam al-Nawawi to clarify the orthodox position. Understanding this foundation is essential before discussing the deviant views.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic definition and its translation. Notice the linguistic derivation and the technical shift.
The word 'qadar' comes from measuring or determining.
2
Understand Imam al-Nawawi's explanation
Identify the two key points: Allah's pre-eternal determination and His knowledge of the specific times and attributes of events.
3
Contrast with the Qadariyya
Even though the Qadariyya are not fully described until the next lesson, note that the passage mentions their denial as a contrast.
This sets up the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَصْلُ (الْقَدَرِ) بِتَحْرِيكِ الدَّالِ وَتَسْكِينِهَا، مَصْدَرُ قَدَرْتُ الشَّيْءَ بِفَتْحِ الدَّالِ وَتَخْفِيفِهَا إِذَا أَحَطْتَ بِمِقْدَارِهِ أَيْ حَقِيقَتِهِ (سِرُّ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى) أَيْ عِلْمُهُ بِمَا يَكُونُ (فِي خَلْقِهِ) ثُمَّ إِيجَادُهُ مَا سَبَقَ فِي عِلْمِهِ أَنَّهُ يُوجَدُ، وَيُعَبَّرُ عَنْ هَذَا بِقَضَائِهِ. قَالَ الْإِمَامُ النَّوَوِيُّ فِي شَرْحِهِ عَلَى صَحِيحِ الْإِمَامِ مُسْلِمٍ: اعْلَمْ أَنَّ مَذْهَبَ أَهْلِ السُّنَّةِ إِثْبَاتُ الْقَدَرِ، وَهُوَ أَنَّهُ سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى قَدَّرَ الْأَشْيَاءَ فِي الْقِدَمِ وَعَلِمَ سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى أَنَّهَا سَتَقَعُ فِي أَوْقَاتٍ مَعْلُومَةٍ عِنْدَهُ تَعَالَى وَعَلَى صِفَاتٍ مَخْصُوصَةٍ؛ فَهِيَ تَقَعُ عَلَى حَسَبِ مَا قَدَّرَهَا سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى، وَأَنْكَرَتِ الْقَدَرِيَّةُ هَذَا وَزَعَمَتْ أَنَّهُ سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى لَمْ يُقَدِّرْهَا فِي سَابِقِ عِلْمِهِ وَأَنَّهَا مُسْتَأْنَفَةُ الْعِلْمِ؛ أَيْ يَعْلَمُهَا سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى بَعْدَ وُقُوعِهَا؛ تَعَالَى رَبُّنَا عَنْ أَقْوَالِهِمُ الْبَاطِلَةِ عُلُوًّا كَبِيرًا، وَسُمِّيَتْ هَذِهِ الْفِرْقَةُ الْقَدَرِيَّةَ لِإِنْكَارِهِمِ الْقَدَرَ، وَقَدِ انْقَرَضَتْ هَذِهِ الْفِرْقَةُ، وَصَارَتِ الْقَدَرِيَّةُ فِي هَذَا الزَّمَانِ تَعْتَقِدُ أَنَّ الْخَيْرَ مِنَ اللَّهِ وَالشَّرَّ مِنْ غَيْرِهِ، تَعَالَى اللَّهُ عَنْ ذَلِكَ، قَالَ إِمَامُ الْحَرَمَيْنِ فِي إِرْشَادِهِ: «إِنَّ بَعْضَ الْقَدَرِيَّةِ قَالَ: لَسْنَا بِقَدَرِيَّةٍ بَلْ أَنْتُمُ الْقَدَرِيَّةُ لِاعْتِقَادِكُمْ إِثْبَاتَ الْقَدَرِ، وَهَذِهِ جَهَالَةٌ وَتَوَقُّحٌ؛ فَإِنَّا بِحَمْدِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى نُفَوِّضُ أُمُورَنَا إِلَى اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَنُضِيفُ جَمِيعَ الْأُمُورِ إِلَيْهِ، وَهَؤُلَاءِ الْجَهَلَةُ يُضِيفُونَهَا إِلَى أَنْفُسِهِمْ، وَمُضِيفُ الشَّيْءِ إِلَى نَفْسِهِ أَوْلَى بِأَنْ يُنْسَبَ إِلَيْهِ مِمَّنْ يَعْتَقِدُهُ لِغَيْرِهِ». وَقَدْ قَالَ الْقَدَرِيَّةُ مَجُوسُ هَذِهِ الْأُمَّةِ (١) شَبَّهَهُمْ بِهِمْ لِتَقْسِيمِهِمُ الْخَيْرَ وَالشَّرَّ فِي حُكْمِ الْإِرَادَةِ كَمَا قَسَّمَتِ الْمَجُوسُ الْخَيْرَ إِلَى يَزْدَانَ وَالشَّرَّ إِلَى أَهْرُمَنَ (٢) (٣). كَذَا فِي شَرْحِ الطَّرِيقَةِ وَشَرْحِ الْجَوْهَرَةِ لِلْمُصَنِّفِ (٤) عِنْدَ ذِكْرِ الْقَدَرِ.
The root of 'al-qadar' (with movement of the dal and its silence) is the verbal noun of 'qadartu al-shay'a' (I measured the thing) with fatha of the dal and its lightening, when you have encompassed its measure, i.e., its reality. (It is the secret of Allah Most High) i.e., His knowledge of what will be (in His creation), then His bringing into existence what preceded in His knowledge that it would exist, and this is expressed by His decree (qada'). Imam al-Nawawi said in his commentary on Sahih Muslim: 'Know that the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunna is affirmation of qadar, and it is that He, exalted and glorified, determined the things in pre-eternity, and He, exalted and glorified, knew that they will occur at times known to Him and in specific attributes; so they occur according to what He determined. The Qadariyya denied this and claimed that He, exalted and glorified, did not determine them in His prior knowledge, and that they are of renewed knowledge; i.e., He, exalted and glorified, knows them after their occurrence. Exalted is our Lord above their false statements, a great exaltation. This sect was named 'Qadariyya' for their denial of qadar. This sect has become extinct, and the Qadariyya in this time came to believe that good is from Allah and evil from other than Him. Exalted is Allah above that. Imam al-Haramayn said in his Irshad: 'Some of the Qadariyya said: We are not Qadariyya, rather you are the Qadariyya for your belief in affirming qadar. This is ignorance and impudence. For we, by the praise of Allah Most High, entrust our affairs to Allah Most High and ascribe all things to Him. These ignorant ones ascribe them to themselves, and the one who ascribes a thing to himself is more deserving of being attributed to it than the one who attributes it to other than himself.' And it has been said: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation' (1) – he likened them to them because of their division of good and evil in the ruling of will, just as the Magians divided good to Yazdan and evil to Ahriman (2)(3). Thus in Sharh al-Tariqa and Sharh al-Jawhara by the author (4) when mentioning qadar.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage provides a definition of qadar both linguistically and doctrinally, followed by a refutation of the Qadariyya. The author begins by explaining that the word 'qadar' is derived from the root meaning to measure or determine. Technically, it is defined as Allah's secret knowledge of what will be in creation, and then bringing into existence what He knew would exist, also called His decree (qada'). Then Imam al-Nawawi is quoted to clarify the Ahl al-Sunna position: Allah determined all things in pre-eternity and knows they will occur at specific times and with specific attributes; they occur exactly as determined. The Qadariyya are described as those who denied this, claiming that Allah's knowledge is renewed after events occur. The author notes that the original Qadariyya sect has become extinct, but a later group emerged that believed good is from Allah and evil from other than Him. Imam al-Haramayn is then cited, refuting the claim that those who affirm qadar are the real Qadariyya. He argues that the true attribution is to those who ascribe actions to themselves rather than to Allah. Finally, the hadith calling the Qadariyya the 'Magians of this nation' is mentioned, explaining that they resemble the Magians in dividing good and evil between two sources.

قضاء

Key Takeaway
Qadar is Allah's pre-eternal determination and knowledge of all events, and Ahl al-Sunna affirm that all things occur exactly as decreed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every event in your life—including your sins and mistakes—was decreed by Allah in pre-eternity? If so, how does this belief affect your attitude when you are tested with hardship or when you commit a sin? Do you feel resigned or motivated to strive and repent?
?
Consider a moment when something unexpected happened—something you felt was unfair or unjust. Would you respond differently if you fully internalized that it occurred by Allah's exact decree? What would that look like in your heart and actions today?
?
The lesson teaches that qadar is Allah's secret knowledge. Are you comfortable not knowing the future, trusting that Allah's knowledge is perfect? Or do you find yourself anxious or controlling, trying to uncover what is hidden? What would change if you surrendered to that truth right now?

Refutation of the Qadariyya and Their Misconceptions
Maydani refutes the Qadariyya and cites Imam al-Haramayn and the hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Qadariyya's errors, why they are refuted, and the hadith likening them to the Magians.

Core Idea
The Qadariyya deny Allah's prior knowledge and later split good and evil from Him.

After establishing the correct belief in qadar, the author turns to refute those who opposed it. This lesson covers the Qadariyya's claims, the response of Imam al-Haramayn, and the famous prophetic saying that compares them to the Magians. It clarifies why they are not to be followed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Qadariyya's claim
They denied that Allah predetermined events in His prior knowledge and claimed He only knows them after they occur.
This is a serious error about Allah's attribute of knowledge.
2
Understand Imam al-Haramayn's refutation
The Qadariyya argued that those who affirm qadar are the real Qadariyya. Imam al-Haramayn refutes this by showing that the true Qadariyya ascribe actions to themselves, not to Allah.
3
Reflect on the hadith comparison
The Prophet likened the Qadariyya to the Magians for dividing good and evil between two sources, similar to the dualism of Yazdan and Ahriman.
This highlights the gravity of their error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَصْلُ (الْقَدَرِ) بِتَحْرِيكِ الدَّالِ وَتَسْكِينِهَا، مَصْدَرُ قَدَرْتُ الشَّيْءَ بِفَتْحِ الدَّالِ وَتَخْفِيفِهَا إِذَا أَحَطْتَ بِمِقْدَارِهِ أَيْ حَقِيقَتِهِ (سِرُّ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى) أَيْ عِلْمُهُ بِمَا يَكُونُ (فِي خَلْقِهِ) ثُمَّ إِيجَادُهُ مَا سَبَقَ فِي عِلْمِهِ أَنَّهُ يُوجَدُ، وَيُعَبَّرُ عَنْ هَذَا بِقَضَائِهِ. قَالَ الْإِمَامُ النَّوَوِيُّ فِي شَرْحِهِ عَلَى صَحِيحِ الْإِمَامِ مُسْلِمٍ: اعْلَمْ أَنَّ مَذْهَبَ أَهْلِ السُّنَّةِ إِثْبَاتُ الْقَدَرِ، وَهُوَ أَنَّهُ سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى قَدَّرَ الْأَشْيَاءَ فِي الْقِدَمِ وَعَلِمَ سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى أَنَّهَا سَتَقَعُ فِي أَوْقَاتٍ مَعْلُومَةٍ عِنْدَهُ تَعَالَى وَعَلَى صِفَاتٍ مَخْصُوصَةٍ؛ فَهِيَ تَقَعُ عَلَى حَسَبِ مَا قَدَّرَهَا سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى، وَأَنْكَرَتِ الْقَدَرِيَّةُ هَذَا وَزَعَمَتْ أَنَّهُ سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى لَمْ يُقَدِّرْهَا فِي سَابِقِ عِلْمِهِ وَأَنَّهَا مُسْتَأْنَفَةُ الْعِلْمِ؛ أَيْ يَعْلَمُهَا سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى بَعْدَ وُقُوعِهَا؛ تَعَالَى رَبُّنَا عَنْ أَقْوَالِهِمُ الْبَاطِلَةِ عُلُوًّا كَبِيرًا، وَسُمِّيَتْ هَذِهِ الْفِرْقَةُ الْقَدَرِيَّةَ لِإِنْكَارِهِمِ الْقَدَرَ، وَقَدِ انْقَرَضَتْ هَذِهِ الْفِرْقَةُ، وَصَارَتِ الْقَدَرِيَّةُ فِي هَذَا الزَّمَانِ تَعْتَقِدُ أَنَّ الْخَيْرَ مِنَ اللَّهِ وَالشَّرَّ مِنْ غَيْرِهِ، تَعَالَى اللَّهُ عَنْ ذَلِكَ، قَالَ إِمَامُ الْحَرَمَيْنِ فِي إِرْشَادِهِ: «إِنَّ بَعْضَ الْقَدَرِيَّةِ قَالَ: لَسْنَا بِقَدَرِيَّةٍ بَلْ أَنْتُمُ الْقَدَرِيَّةُ لِاعْتِقَادِكُمْ إِثْبَاتَ الْقَدَرِ، وَهَذِهِ جَهَالَةٌ وَتَوَقُّحٌ؛ فَإِنَّا بِحَمْدِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى نُفَوِّضُ أُمُورَنَا إِلَى اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَنُضِيفُ جَمِيعَ الْأُمُورِ إِلَيْهِ، وَهَؤُلَاءِ الْجَهَلَةُ يُضِيفُونَهَا إِلَى أَنْفُسِهِمْ، وَمُضِيفُ الشَّيْءِ إِلَى نَفْسِهِ أَوْلَى بِأَنْ يُنْسَبَ إِلَيْهِ مِمَّنْ يَعْتَقِدُهُ لِغَيْرِهِ». وَقَدْ قَالَ الْقَدَرِيَّةُ مَجُوسُ هَذِهِ الْأُمَّةِ (١) شَبَّهَهُمْ بِهِمْ لِتَقْسِيمِهِمُ الْخَيْرَ وَالشَّرَّ فِي حُكْمِ الْإِرَادَةِ كَمَا قَسَّمَتِ الْمَجُوسُ الْخَيْرَ إِلَى يَزْدَانَ وَالشَّرَّ إِلَى أَهْرُمَنَ (٢) (٣). كَذَا فِي شَرْحِ الطَّرِيقَةِ وَشَرْحِ الْجَوْهَرَةِ لِلْمُصَنِّفِ (٤) عِنْدَ ذِكْرِ الْقَدَرِ.
The root of 'al-qadar' (with movement of the dal and its silence) is the verbal noun of 'qadartu al-shay'a' (I measured the thing) with fatha of the dal and its lightening, when you have encompassed its measure, i.e., its reality. (It is the secret of Allah Most High) i.e., His knowledge of what will be (in His creation), then His bringing into existence what preceded in His knowledge that it would exist, and this is expressed by His decree (qada'). Imam al-Nawawi said in his commentary on Sahih Muslim: 'Know that the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunna is affirmation of qadar, and it is that He, exalted and glorified, determined the things in pre-eternity, and He, exalted and glorified, knew that they will occur at times known to Him and in specific attributes; so they occur according to what He determined. The Qadariyya denied this and claimed that He, exalted and glorified, did not determine them in His prior knowledge, and that they are of renewed knowledge; i.e., He, exalted and glorified, knows them after their occurrence. Exalted is our Lord above their false statements, a great exaltation. This sect was named 'Qadariyya' for their denial of qadar. This sect has become extinct, and the Qadariyya in this time came to believe that good is from Allah and evil from other than Him. Exalted is Allah above that. Imam al-Haramayn said in his Irshad: 'Some of the Qadariyya said: We are not Qadariyya, rather you are the Qadariyya for your belief in affirming qadar. This is ignorance and impudence. For we, by the praise of Allah Most High, entrust our affairs to Allah Most High and ascribe all things to Him. These ignorant ones ascribe them to themselves, and the one who ascribes a thing to himself is more deserving of being attributed to it than the one who attributes it to other than himself.' And it has been said: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation' (1) – he likened them to them because of their division of good and evil in the ruling of will, just as the Magians divided good to Yazdan and evil to Ahriman (2)(3). Thus in Sharh al-Tariqa and Sharh al-Jawhara by the author (4) when mentioning qadar.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage provides a definition of qadar both linguistically and doctrinally, followed by a refutation of the Qadariyya. The author begins by explaining that the word 'qadar' is derived from the root meaning to measure or determine. Technically, it is defined as Allah's secret knowledge of what will be in creation, and then bringing into existence what He knew would exist, also called His decree (qada'). Then Imam al-Nawawi is quoted to clarify the Ahl al-Sunna position: Allah determined all things in pre-eternity and knows they will occur at specific times and with specific attributes; they occur exactly as determined. The Qadariyya are described as those who denied this, claiming that Allah's knowledge is renewed after events occur. The author notes that the original Qadariyya sect has become extinct, but a later group emerged that believed good is from Allah and evil from other than Him. Imam al-Haramayn is then cited, refuting the claim that those who affirm qadar are the real Qadariyya. He argues that the true attribution is to those who ascribe actions to themselves rather than to Allah. Finally, the hadith calling the Qadariyya the 'Magians of this nation' is mentioned, explaining that they resemble the Magians in dividing good and evil between two sources.

Definitions of Qadar in Maturidi and Ash'ari Thought
Maydani presents and reconciles the Maturidi and Ash'ari definitions of qadar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi and Ash'ari definitions of qadar and how they are essentially in agreement despite different wording.

Core Idea
Differences in qadar definitions are verbal, not doctrinal.

The concept of qadar (divine decree) is central to Islamic theology, yet different schools express it differently. In this passage, Maydani presents the definitions of the Maturidi and Ash'ari schools and shows that they are reconcilable. Understanding this helps avoid harsh sectarian disputes and focuses on the core belief that Allah's knowledge encompasses all things.

Guided Path
1
Read the Maturidi definition
Start by reading the first part of the passage which defines qadar according to the Maturidis. Note the emphasis on Allah's eternal determination of every thing's limit, goodness, time, place, and consequences.
The definition is comprehensive, covering both physical and moral dimensions.
2
Read the Ash'ari definition
Then read the Ash'ari definition as given by al-Sayyid al-Sharif. Compare it to the Maturidi one. Notice that it speaks of Allah bringing things into existence upon a specific measure and determination.
3
Understand the reconciliation
Finally, read the author's reconciliation and the quote from Imam al-Nawawi. See how the author argues that the difference is only in wording and that both schools ultimately refer to Allah's knowledge of His creation.
Highlight the phrase 'وَأَنَّ الْمُرَادَ عِلْمُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى بِإِيجَادِهِ الْأَشْيَاءَ' (the intended meaning is Allah's knowledge in bringing things into existence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَهُوَ (ه) عِنْدَ الْمَاتُرِيدِيَّةِ: تَحْدِيدُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى أَزَلًا كُلَّ مَخْلُودٍ (كَذَا) بِحَدِّهِ الَّذِي يُوجَدُ بِهِ مِنْ حُسْنٍ وَقُبْحٍ وَنَفْعٍ وَخَيْرٍ وَمَا يَحْوِيهِ مِنْ زَمَانٍ وَمَكَانٍ وَمَا يَتَرَتَّبُ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ طَاعَةٍ وَعِصْيَانٍ وَثَوَابٍ وَعِقَابٍ أَوْ غُفْرَانٍ وَنَحْوِهِ، قَالَ بَعْضُهُمُ: الْمُرَادُ مِنَ الْقَدَرِ أَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى عَلِمَ مَقَادِيرَ الْأَشْيَاءِ وَأَزْمَانَهَا قَبْلَ إِيجَادِهَا ثُمَّ أَوْجَدَ مَا سَبَقَ فِي عِلْمِهِ أَنَّهُ يُوجَدُ؛ فَكُلُّ مُحْدَثٍ صَادِرٌ عَنْ عِلْمِهِ وَقُدْرَتِهِ وَإِرَادَتِهِ، هَذَا هُوَ الْمَعْلُومُ مِنَ الدِّينِ بِقَوَاطِعِ الْبَرَاهِينِ وَعَلَيْهِ كَانَ السَّلَفُ مِنَ الصَّحَابَةِ وَخِيَارُ التَّابِعِينَ قَبْلَ حُدُوثِ الْقَدَرِيَّةِ الْمُخَالِفِينَ. وَعِنْدَ الْأَشَاعِرَةِ إِيجَادُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى الْأَشْيَاءَ عَلَى قَدْرٍ مَخْصُوصٍ وَتَقْدِيرٍ مُعَيَّنٍ فِي ذَوَاتِهَا وَأَحْوَالِهَا، كَمَا نَسَبَهُ لَهُمُ السَّيِّدُ فِي شَرْحِ الْمَوَاقِفِ (٦). وَالظَّاهِرُ أَنَّهُ اخْتِلَافُ عِبَارَةٍ وَأَنَّ الْمُرَادَ عِلْمُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى بِإِيجَادِهِ الْأَشْيَاءَ؛ أَلَا تَرَى إِلَى عِبَارَةِ النَّوَوِيِّ - نَفَعَنَا اللَّهُ بِهِ - وَهُوَ مِنْهُمْ حَيْثُ قَالَ: وَمَعْنَاهُ أَنَّ اللَّهَ قَدَّرَ الْأَشْيَاءَ فِي الْقِدَمِ وَعَلِمَ سُبْحَانَهُ أَنَّهَا سَتَقَعُ فِي أَوْقَاتٍ مَعْلُومَةٍ عِنْدَهُ وَعَلَى صِفَاتٍ
And it (qadar) according to the Maturidis is: Allah Most High's eternal determination of every created thing by its limit with which it exists, of goodness and ugliness, benefit and good, and what it contains of time and place, and what follows from it of obedience and disobedience, reward and punishment, or forgiveness and the like. Some of them said: The intended meaning of qadar is that Allah Most High knew the measures of things and their times before bringing them into existence, then brought into existence what had preceded in His knowledge that it would exist. So every originated thing issues from His knowledge, power, and will. This is what is known of the religion by decisive proofs, and upon this were the Salaf from the Companions and the best of the Followers before the emergence of the opposing Qadariyya. And according to the Ash'aris it is: Allah Most High's bringing things into existence upon a specific measure and a particular determination in their essences and states, as al-Sayyid attributed to them in Sharh al-Mawaqif (6). And the apparent is that it is a difference in expression and that the intended meaning is Allah Most High's knowledge in bringing things into existence. Do you not see the expression of al-Nawawi – may Allah benefit us by him – and he is one of them, where he said: 'And its meaning is that Allah determined the things in pre-eternity and He, glorified, knew that they will occur at times known to Him and upon attributes'
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage presents and reconciles the definitions of qadar according to the Maturidi and Ash'ari schools. The author first states the Maturidi definition: qadar is Allah's eternal determination of every created thing with its specific limit, encompassing all aspects of its existence, including moral qualities, temporal and spatial dimensions, and consequences. A summarised definition is then given: Allah knew the measures and times of things before creation and then created accordingly; everything originates from His knowledge, power, and will. The author asserts that this is the established doctrine known by decisive proofs and held by the Salaf. Next, the Ash'ari definition is given: Allah brings things into existence upon a specific measure and determination in their essences and states, as attributed to them by al-Sayyid al-Sharif in Sharh al-Mawaqif. The author then reconciles the two, stating that the difference is merely verbal, as both ultimately refer to Allah's knowledge of His bringing things into existence. He supports this by quoting Imam al-Nawawi, who, despite being Ash'ari, gives a definition that aligns with the Maturidi understanding – that Allah determined things in pre-eternity and knew they would occur at known times and with attributes.

Key Terms
قدر
ماتريدية
أشاعرة
سلف
إمام النووي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Maturidi and Ash'ari positions on qadar are fundamentally different.
Correction: The passage shows they are in agreement; the difference is only in wording.

Checkpoint
How does the author reconcile the Maturidi and Ash'ari definitions of qadar?
A) He rejects the Ash'ari definition
B) He says the difference is only in wording and both refer to Allah's knowledge
C) He prefers the Maturidi definition
D) He declares both definitions to be incorrect

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi and Ash'ari definitions of qadar are essentially the same; the difference is one of expression, not doctrine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage shows that two schools often thought to be in conflict actually agree on qadar. Are you quick to divide the Ummah based on verbal differences, or do you seek the underlying unity? What label do you cling to that might be obscuring the truth that others also hold?
?
Imam al-Nawawi, despite being Ash'ari, expressed qadar in a way that matches the Maturidi definition. When you study a disputed issue, do you truly aim to understand the position of the other side, or do you merely defend your own school? Can you point to a time you changed your view after realizing a difference was merely verbal?
?
The Salaf held this belief before the Qadariyya emerged. How embedded is your conviction in qadar? If you were tested with trials tomorrow, would your heart still rest on the knowledge that everything is from Allah's wise decree, or would you question His justice? What one habit can you adopt today to strengthen your reliance on qadar?

Definition of Qadar According to the Maturidis
Definition of Qadar according to Maturidis with hadith on Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi definition of Qadar as Allah's eternal determination of all creatures and its basis in divine knowledge, power, and will.

Core Idea
Qadar is Allah's eternal determination of everything, not just human actions.

This passage defines the term Qadar as understood by the Maturidi school, grounding it in divine attributes and refuting the Qadariyya misconception. The hadith comparing Qadariyya to Magians sets the stage for understanding the correct Islamic position.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its explanation
Read the opening hadith comparing Qadariyya to Magians and the reason for the comparison. Understand that the Qadariyya divided good and evil in divine will, similar to the Magian dualism.
This hadith is a prophetic warning against those who deny divine predestination.
2
Understand the Maturidi definition
Read the definition: 'Allah's eternal determination of every creature to its limit.' Reflect on how it encompasses all aspects of existence and actions.
The definition is comprehensive, covering good, bad, time, place, and outcomes.
3
Consider the explanation about divine knowledge
Some scholars explain that Qadar is based on Allah's eternal knowledge of measures and times before creation, and that everything proceeds from His knowledge, power, and will.
This reinforces that Qadar is not arbitrary but rooted in divine wisdom.
4
Recognize the authority of the Salaf
Note that this understanding is established by decisive proofs and was the creed of the Salaf (Companions and Followers) before the emergence of the Qadariyya.
This shows that the Maturidi position is the orthodox Sunni view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال القَدَرِيَّةُ تَجُوسُ هَذِهِ الأُمَّةِ» (۱) شبههم بهم لتقسيمهم الخير والشر في حكم الإرادة كما قسمت المجوس الخير إلى يزدان والشر إلى أهر من (۲) (۳). كذا في شرح الطريقة وشرح الجوهرة للمصنف (٤) عند ذكر القدر. وهو (ه) عند الماتريدية: تحديد الله تعالى أزلا كل مخلوق بحده الذي يوجد به من حسن وقبح ونفع وخير وما يحويه من زمان ومكان وما يترتب عليه من طاعة وعصيان وثواب وعقاب أو غفران ونحوه، قال بعضهم: المراد من القدر أن الله تعالى علم مقادير الأشياء وأزمانها قبل إيجادها ثم أوجد ما سبق في علمه أنه يوجد؛ فكل محدث صادر عن علمه وقدرته وإرادته، هذا هو المعلوم من الدين بقواطع البراهين وعليه كان السلف من الصحابة وخيار التابعين قبل حدوث القدرية المخالفين.
He said: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this ummah' (1) likening them to them because they divide good and evil in the rule of will just as the Magians divided good into Yazdan and evil into Ahriman (2) (3). Likewise in Sharh al-Tariqa and Sharh al-Jawhara by the author (4) when mentioning Qadar. And it (5) according to the Maturidis: Allah's eternal determination of every creature to its limit by which it exists, from good and bad, benefit and good, and what it contains of time and place, and what results from it of obedience and disobedience, reward and punishment, or forgiveness and similar. Some said: The meaning of Qadar is that Allah, exalted, knew the measures of things and their times before bringing them into existence, then He brought into existence what preceded in His knowledge that it would exist; so every originated thing proceeds from His knowledge, power, and will. This is what is known of the religion by decisive proofs, and upon this were the Salaf among the Companions and the best of the Followers before the emergence of the opposing Qadariyya.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage begins by citing a hadith that the Qadariyya are the Magians of this ummah. It explains that the comparison is because they divide good and evil in the realm of divine will, just as the Magians attributed good to Yazdan and evil to Ahriman. The author then references explanations from other works. He then presents the Maturidi definition of Qadar: it is Allah's eternal determination of every creature to its specific limit encompassing all aspects of its existence and actions. Some scholars explain that Qadar means Allah's eternal knowledge of the measures and times of things before their creation, and that He then creates them according to that knowledge. The passage concludes that this understanding is established by decisive proofs and was the creed of the Salaf before the emergence of the Qadariyya who opposed it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qadariyya believed that good and evil come from separate sources, like the Magians.
Correction: Islam teaches that both good and evil are under Allah's will and determination.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidis, what is the meaning of Qadar (divine decree)?
A) Allah's creation of things without any prior determination.
B) Allah's eternal determination of every creature to its specific limit, known by His knowledge and executed by His power and will.
C) The belief that good comes from Allah and evil comes from something else.
D) A concept that only concerns human actions without affecting the rest of creation.

Key Takeaway
Qadar is Allah's eternal determination of all creatures, known by His knowledge and executed by His power and will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?
The Salaf believed this creed before the emergence of the Qadariyya. Are you content to follow their path, or do you find yourself tempted to reject parts of Allah's decree? Will you commit to learning the proofs of this belief so that your heart rests in submission?

The Ash'ari Definition of Qadar and the Verbal-Real Difference
Ash'ari definition of Qadar and the verbal/real difference debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari definition of Qadar and the theological debate over whether it differs from the Maturidi view in substance or only in wording.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari definition of Qadar may be the same as the Maturidi wording, but a real difference lies beneath.

This passage presents the Ash'ari definition of Qadar and then discusses whether it is merely a verbal variation from the Maturidi definition or a substantive theological disagreement. The text explores this by citing al-Nawawi's formulation, which reduces the difference to knowledge, and then notes that some scholars consider the difference real, based on the attributes of action.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the full translation. Note the key terms and the flow from definition to discussion.
The passage is short but dense. Read carefully.
2
Identify the Ash'ari definition and compare with Maturidi
The Ash'ari definition is given as 'إيجاد الله تعالى الأشياء على قدر مخصوص وتقدير معين'. Compare this to the Maturidi definition (from earlier lessons) to see the similarity.
The author suggests the difference might be just wording.
3
Analyze the two positions on the difference
Notice that al-Nawawi's explanation frames Qadar as God's knowledge, supporting a verbal difference. Then see that Abd al-Ghani al-Matlabi holds the difference is real, tied to whether attributes of action are eternal or originated.
This connects to deeper theology of God's attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعند الأشاعرة إيجاد الله تعالى الأشياء على قدر مخصوص وتقدير معين في ذواتها وأحوالها، كما نسبه لهم السيد في شرح المواقف (٦). والظاهر أنه اختلاف عبارة وأن المراد علم الله تعالى بإيجاده الأشياء؛ ألا ترى إلى عبارة النووي - نفعنا الله بـه - وهو منهم حيث قال: ومعناه أن الله قدر الأشياء في القدم وعلم سبحانه أنها ستقع في أوقات معلومة عنده وعلى صفات مخصوصة؛ فهي تقع على حسب ما قدرها (۱) اهـ لكن استظهر سيدي عبد الغني في المطالب أن الخلاف ،معنوي، وأنه مبني على الخلاف في صفات الفعل قدما وحدوتا فراجعه (۲).
And according to the Ash'aris: Allah bringing things into existence on a specific measure and a particular determination in their essences and states, as attributed to them by al-Sayyid in Sharh al-Mawaqif (6). And it appears that it is a verbal difference and that the intended meaning is Allah's knowledge through His bringing things into existence. Do you not see the statement of al-Nawawi - may Allah benefit us with him - and he is one of them, where he said: Its meaning is that Allah determined the things in eternity and knew that they will occur at times known to Him and on specific attributes; so they occur according to what He determined (1). End quote. But my master Abd al-Ghani al-Matlabi held that the difference is real, and that it is based on the difference regarding the attributes of action being eternal or originated, so refer to it (2).
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage presents the Ash'ari definition of Qadar: it is Allah's bringing of things into existence on a specific measure and determination in their essences and states. The author then notes that this appears to be a verbal difference with the Maturidi definition, because the intended meaning is ultimately Allah's knowledge in bringing things into existence. He supports this by quoting Imam al-Nawawi, who states that Qadar means Allah determined things in eternity and knew that they would occur at specific times and attributes. However, the commentator Abd al-Ghani al-Matlabi is said to have held that the difference is real, not merely verbal, and that it is based on the broader issue of whether the attributes of action are eternal or created. The author therefore directs the reader to consult that discussion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Maturidi and Ash'ari definitions of Qadar are exactly the same in all respects.
Correction: While they appear similar, some scholars argue that the difference is real, based on whether God's attributes of action are eternal or created.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Ash'ari definition of Qadar?
A) Allah's eternal determination of creatures to their limits.
B) Allah bringing things into existence on a specific measure and determination.
C) The belief that Allah only knows without determining.
D) The division of good and evil to two sources.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari definition of Qadar is Allah bringing things into existence on a specific measure, but whether this differs from the Maturidi view is debated; the real disagreement concerns the nature of God's attributes of action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

This lesson shows that a simple verbal difference can hide a profound issue about who God is. Will you commit to digging deeper the next time you encounter a seemingly minor dispute in Islamic theology?
?

?

How does that affect your trust in Him today?

The Warning Against Investigating Qadar and the Proof of Kufr
Imam al-Tahawi warns against investigating Qadar and presents a syllogism proving that questioning it leads to disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why delving into the mystery of Qadar is forbidden and how questioning it constitutes rejection of the Quran, leading to disbelief.

Core Idea
Questioning Qadar is not just risky—it is a form of rejecting the Quran itself.

This passage from Imam al-Tahawi's creed warns believers against trying to uncover the secret of divine decree. It explains that even prophets and angels have not been given this knowledge, and that attempting to do so leads to spiritual ruin. The author then links questioning Qadar to rejecting the Quran, making it a matter of faith and disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Let the author's words sink in before analyzing.
Notice the strong warnings and the logical structure at the end.
2
Understand the secret of Qadar
The author states that no angel or prophet has been given knowledge of this secret. This demonstrates human inability and the exclusivity of Allah's knowledge.
3
Identify the consequences
The passage lists khidhlan (forsaken by Allah), deprivation of faith, and transgression as results of investigating Qadar. Recognize these as warnings.
These are not mere possibilities but certain outcomes.
4
Grasp the Quranic proof and syllogism
The author quotes Quran 21:23 and then argues that questioning 'why' is rejecting the Quran, which is kufr. Understand how the syllogism works.
This is a conjunctive syllogism of the first figure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم يطلع على ذلك السر الذي أسره سبحانه وتعالى (ملك مقرب ولا نبي مرسل إظهارًا لعجز من اتصف بالعبودية عن درك ما استبدت به الذات الأحدية، والتعمق والنظر في ذلك) لإدراكه ذريعة) أي وسيلة (الخذلان) بالضم: ترك العون والنصرة، وسلم الحرمان) عن الثبات على صحيح الإيمان ( ودرجة) أي مرقاة (الطغيان) أي الزلل عما عليه الراسخون أهل العرفان فالحذر ) أي الحذر كل الحذر من ذلك نظرًا أو فكرًا أو وسوسة)؛ فإن ذلك من مكائد الشيطان؛ فمتى خَلَجَ في خاطرك فاستعذ منه بالرحمن، وفوض العلم لعالمه بالتصديق والإذعان؛ فإن الله تعالى) قد (طوى علم القدر عن جميع (أنامه) أي خلقه ونهاهم عن مرامه) أي طلبه ( كما قال في محكم كتابه) : لَا يُسْتَلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ وَهُمْ يُسْتَلُونَ ) (سورة الأنبياء آية: 23]؛ فمن سأل: لم فعل ؟ فقد وقع في الزلل؛ لأنه قد رد حكم كتاب الله تعالى (ومن رد حكم كتاب الله تعالى كان من الكافرين)؛ فهذا قياس اقتراني (٣) من الشكل الأول (٤) كل من رد حكم كتاب الله تعالى كان من الكافرين
That secret which Allah, glorified and exalted, has concealed was not disclosed to (any close angel nor any sent prophet) as a manifestation of the inability of one characterized by servitude to grasp what the Unique Essence has exclusively controlled. And delving deeply and reflecting on that is a means (of abandonment) – i.e., a cause of being forsaken (khidhlan) meaning: withholding of aid and victory – and a ladder of deprivation from steadfastness on sound faith, and a degree – i.e., a step – of transgression – i.e., deviation from what the firmly grounded people of gnosis are upon. So beware – i.e., be completely wary of that, whether by thought, reflection, or whispering; for indeed that is from the snares of Satan. So when it occurs in your mind, seek refuge from it with the Most Merciful, and entrust knowledge to its Knower with affirmation and submission. Indeed Allah, exalted, has concealed the knowledge of Qadar from all His creatures and forbade them from seeking it, as He said in His decisive Book: 'He is not questioned about what He does, but they will be questioned' (Surah al-Anbiya 21:23). So whoever asks: Why did He do? has indeed fallen into error; because he has rejected the ruling of the Book of Allah (and whoever rejects the ruling of the Book of Allah is one of the disbelievers). So this is a conjunctive syllogism (qiyas iqtirani) of the first figure: Everyone who rejects the ruling of the Book of Allah is one of the disbelievers.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a warning against seeking to understand the secret of Qadar. It begins by stating that no angel or prophet has been made aware of this secret, as a demonstration of human inability. It then describes that engaging in such inquiry leads to khidhlan (being forsaken by Allah), deprivation of steadfast faith, and transgression. The reader is warned to avoid even thinking about it, as it is a trap of Satan. The solution is to seek refuge and to entrust knowledge to Allah. The passage quotes the Quranic verse (21:23) that Allah is not questioned about His actions. It then draws a logical conclusion: anyone who asks 'why did He do?' has rejected the ruling of the Quran, and rejection of the Quran is kufr. This is presented as a conjunctive syllogism (qiyas iqtirani) of the first figure, with the major premise being that whoever rejects the Quran is a disbeliever.

Key Terms
السر
الخذلان
الحرمان
الطغيان
القياس الاقتراني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that questioning Qadar is permissible as long as it is not open rejection.
Correction: The passage shows that the act of questioning itself is considered rejecting the Quran, which is kufr.

Checkpoint

A) It is a permissible question to seek understanding.
B) It leads to falling into error and rejection of the Quran, which is kufr.
C) It shows intelligence and piety.
D) It is recommended to ask such questions.

Key Takeaway
To question divine decree is to reject the Quran, which constitutes disbelief.

The Prohibition of Questioning Divine Decree: A Logical Proof
Imam Maydani warns against probing qadar and proves its prohibition syllogistically.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why probing the secret of divine decree is prohibited and how Imam Maydani proves this using a conjunctive syllogism of the first figure.

Core Idea
Questioning why God does what He does leads to disbelief, as proven by a self-evident syllogism.

Imam Maydani presents a stern warning against delving into the hidden secret of divine decree (qadar). He not only forbids it but also provides a logical proof using a syllogism. This lesson unpacks that proof and explains why such inquiry is considered a rejection of Allah's Book.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its full literal translation. Let the author's warning and proof structure sink in before analysis.
Notice the emphatic tone in the warning.
2
Identify the Quranic evidence
Find the Quranic verse cited (Quran 21:23) and understand how it is used as the foundation of the syllogism.
The verse states that Allah is not questioned about what He does.
3
Analyze the syllogism
Break down the syllogism: identify the implicit major premise (whoever rejects Allah's Book is a disbeliever), the explicit minor premise (asking 'Why did He do?' is rejecting the Book), and the conclusion.
The author explicitly calls it a conjunctive syllogism (qiyas iqtirani) of the first figure.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this warning is so severe: questioning divine decree is equivalent to rejecting the Quran and thus leads to disbelief.
This explains the gravity of probing qadar without proper submission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم يطلع على ذلك السر الذي أسره سبحانه وتعالى (ملك مقرب ولا نبي مرسل) إظهارًا لعجز من اتصف بالعبودية عن درك ما استبدت به الذات الأحدية، والتعمق والنظر في ذلك (لإدراكه ذريعة) أي وسيلة (الخذلان) بالضم: ترك العون والنصرة، و (سلم الحرمان) عن الثبات على صحيح الإيمان و (درجة) أي مرقاة (الطغيان) أي الزلل عما عليه الراسخون أهل العرفان فالحذر ) أي الحذر كل الحذر من ذلك نظرًا أو فكرًا أو وسوسة)؛ فإن ذلك من مكائد الشيطان؛ فمتى خَلَجَ في خاطرك فاستعذ منه بالرحمن، وفوض العلم لعالمه بالتصديق والإذعان؛ فإن الله تعالى قد (طوى علم القدر عن جميع (أنامه) أي خلقه ونهاهم عن مرامه) أي طلبه ( كما قال في محكم كتابه) : لَا يُسْأَلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ وَهُمْ يُسْأَلُونَ (سورة الأنبياء آية: ٢٣)؛ فمن سأل: لم فعل؟ فقد وقع في الزلل؛ لأنه قد رد حكم كتاب الله تعالى (ومن رد حكم كتاب الله تعالى كان من الكافرين)؛ فهذا قياس اقتراني من الشكل الأول كل من مقدمتيه بديهي التسليم فينتج مسلما: من سأل لم فعل؟ كان من الكافرين.
Neither a close angel nor a sent prophet has attained that secret which Allah the Exalted kept hidden, as a manifestation of the incapacity of those described by servitude to grasp what the Unique Essence has reserved for Itself. And deep investigation and reflection on that (is a means) i.e. a cause of (abandonment) with damm: cessation of aid and support, and (the ladder of deprivation) from steadfastness upon correct faith, and (a degree) i.e. a step of (transgression) i.e. slipping from what the firmly grounded people of gnosis are upon. So beware, i.e. be completely cautious of that, whether by looking, thinking, or whispering; for that is from the snares of Satan. So whenever it occurs to your mind, seek refuge from it with the Most Merciful, and delegate knowledge to its Knower with affirmation and submission. For Allah the Exalted has (folded up the knowledge of divine decree from all His (creatures) i.e. His creation, and forbade them from seeking it) i.e. pursuing it, as He said in His firm Book: 'He is not questioned about what He does, but they are questioned' (Surah al-Anbiya, verse 23). So whoever asks 'Why did He do?' has indeed fallen into error; because he has rejected the ruling of Allah's Book. (And whoever rejects the ruling of Allah's Book is among the disbelievers). So this is a conjunctive syllogism of the first figure, each of its two premises being self-evidently conceded, so it yields as a conceded conclusion: whoever asks 'Why did He do?' is among the disbelievers.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a theological warning and a proof. The author begins by stating that the secret of divine decree (qadar) is hidden from all creatures, including angels and prophets, to demonstrate the incapacity of servants. He then warns against delving into it through thought or whisper, as it is a satanic trap. He instructs to seek refuge and submit to Allah. He cites the Quranic verse that Allah is not questioned about His actions. He then constructs a syllogism: the major premise (implicit) is that whoever rejects the ruling of Allah's Book is a disbeliever; the minor premise is that whoever asks 'Why did He do?' has rejected the ruling of Allah's Book (because the verse prohibits questioning). The conclusion is that such a person is a disbeliever. He identifies this as a conjunctive syllogism (qiyas iqtirani) of the first figure (al-shakl al-awwal) with self-evidently conceded premises (badihi al-taslim).

Key Terms
القدر
القياس الاقتراني
الشكل الأول
بديهي التسليم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Questioning God's actions is permissible out of curiosity or intellectual pursuit.
Correction: Imam Maydani proves that such questioning is a rejection of Allah's Book and leads to disbelief.

Checkpoint
What is the conclusion of the syllogism presented?
A) The secret of qadar is hidden from all creatures.
B) Whoever asks 'Why did He do?' is among the disbelievers.
C) Deep reflection is a means of abandonment.
D) Only angels know the secret.

Key Takeaway
Questioning Allah's actions regarding divine decree is equivalent to rejecting His Book and leads to disbelief, as proven by a sound syllogism.

What Reaches You Was Not to Miss You
Definition of the core qadar statement and attributes of Allah's decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that whatever Allah decrees for a person must occur, and that His decree is firm and binding with no possibility of change.

Core Idea
Allah's decree is absolute: what missed you was never meant to hit you.

This lesson explains the foundational belief in qadar expressed in the famous phrase: 'What missed the servant was not to hit him, and what hit him was not to miss him.' The author then elaborates on the nature of Allah's prior knowledge and decree, emphasizing that it is unchangeable and all-encompassing. Understanding this brings peace and certainty to the believer's heart.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement
Read the first two sentences carefully. Notice the parallelism and its implication: everything that happens is by Allah's decree.
2
Identify the obligation
The author states it is upon the servant to know two things: Allah's prior knowledge and His firm decree. Find these in the text.
3
Understand the attributes of the decree
The decree is described with several negations: no abrogator, no revoker, etc. Reflect on what each negation means for our belief.

وَمَا أَخْطَأَ العَبْدَ لَمْ يَكُنْ لِيُصِيبَهُ وَمَا أَصَابَهُ لَمْ يَكُنْ لِيُخْطِئَهُ، وَعَلَى العَبْدِ أَنْ يَعْلَمَ أَنَّ اللهَ قَدْ سَبَقَ عِلْمُهُ فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ كَائِنِ مِنْ خَلْقِهِ وَقَدَّرَ ذَلِكَ بِمَشِيئَتِهِ تَقْدِيرًا مُحْكَما مُبْرَمًا لَيْسَ فِيهِ نَاقِضُ وَلَا مُعَقِّبٌ وَلَا مُضِيلٌ وَلَا مُغَيَّرٌ وَلَا تُحَوِّلُ وَلَا زَائِدٌ وَلَا نَاقِصٌ مِنْ خَلْقِهِ فِي سَمَوَاتِهِ وَأَرْضِهِ، وَذَلِكَ مِنْ عَقْدِ الإِيمَانِ وَأُصُولِ الْمَعْرِفَةِ والاعتراف بِتَوْحِيدِ اللهِ وَرُبُوبِيَّتِهِ كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى فِي كِتَابِهِ العَزِيزِ: ﴿وَخَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَقَدَّرَهُ تَقْدِيرًا ﴾ [سورة الفرقان آية: (٢) وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿ وَكَانَ أَمْرُ اللَّهِ قَدَرًا مقدورًا ﴾ [سورة الأحزاب آية: ۳۸]؛ فَوَيْلٌ لَنْ صَارَ لَهُ اللَّهُ فِي القَدَرِ خَصِيّا وَأَحْضَرَ لِلنَّظَرِ فِيهِ قَلْبًا سَقِيها؛ لَقَدِ الْتَمَسَ بِوَهْمِهِ فِي تَحْضِ الغَيبِ سِرًّا كَثِيرًا وَعَادَ بِمَا قَالَ فِيهِ أَنَّاكًا [؟] أَثِيمًا.
What missed the servant was not to hit him, and what hit him was not to miss him. It is upon the servant to know that Allah’s knowledge has preceded in every thing that is brought into existence from His creation, and He decreed that with His will, a firm and binding decree, in which there is no abrogator, nor revoker, nor [one who] leads astray, nor changer, nor [any] alteration, nor increase, nor decrease from His creation in His heavens and His earth. And that is part of the bond of faith and the foundations of knowledge and the acknowledgment of the oneness of Allah and His lordship, as He said in His Mighty Book: 'And He created every thing and determined it with [precise] determination' [Surah al-Furqan: 2], and He said: 'And the command of Allah is a decree determined' [Surah al-Ahzab: 38]. So woe to the one who makes Allah an opponent in qadar and presents for speculation therein a sick heart; he sought with his illusion in the examination of the unseen a great secret and returned with what he said [؟] a sinful.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage explains the Tahawiyyah creedal statement that whatever Allah did not decree to happen to a person will never happen, and whatever He decreed to happen must occur. It then adds the obligation for every servant to believe that Allah's knowledge preceded the existence of everything, and that His decree is firm and binding with no possibility of change, increase, or decrease. This belief is rooted in tawhid and acknowledgment of Allah's lordship. The author then cites two Quranic verses as proof: from Surah al-Furqan (creation and precise decree) and Surah al-Ahzab (the decree is determined). Finally, a severe warning is given to those who dispute qadar with Allah, calling them wicked for seeking hidden secrets through their own illusions.

Key Terms
سبق علمه
تقدير محكم مبرم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that what happens to a person is random or occurs outside of Allah's will.
Correction: This passage clearly states that every occurrence is precisely decreed and that nothing happens without Allah's prior knowledge and decree.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT true about Allah's decree?
A) It is firm and binding
B) It can be changed by prayer
C) It is preceded by Allah's knowledge
D) It encompasses all creation

Key Takeaway
The first lesson of qadar: what Allah decrees must occur, and His decree is unchangeable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a recent disappointment or a missed opportunity. Do you truly believe that it was decreed to miss you and could not have been otherwise? How does this belief affect your emotional response? Will you commit to saying 'Qadr Allah' and moving forward without regret?
?
The decree is described as having no changer or alteration. Are there areas in your life where you secretly wish you could change the past or alter Allah's decree? What does that reveal about your trust in Allah's wisdom? How can you work on accepting His decree completely?
?
Consider the phrase 'what hit you was not to miss you.' When a trial befalls you, do you immediately recognize it as from Allah's decree, or do you look for other causes? How can you train yourself to respond with contentment and reliance on Allah's perfect knowledge?

The Bond of Faith and Warning Against Disputing Qadar
Quranic proofs for decree and warning against disputing it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that believing in Allah's decree is an essential part of faith and tawhid, and that disputing qadar leads to sin.

Core Idea
Belief in divine decree is the very bond of faith; disputing it is a grave sin.

Having established the nature of Allah's decree, the author now places this belief at the core of Islamic faith. He cites two Quranic verses that affirm Allah's creation and precise decree, then delivers a stern warning against those who engage in futile speculation about qadar. This lesson highlights the importance of acceptance and the danger of intellectual arrogance in matters of the unseen.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic proofs
Read the two verses cited. Notice how they support the prior description of decree.
2
Understand the status of this belief
The author says this belief is 'from the bond of faith and foundations of knowledge'. Reflect on why it is so central.
3
Heed the warning
Read the severe warning against those who dispute qadar. What are they accused of? What is the consequence?

Hadith of the Lifted Pens as Proof for Qadar
Citation of the hadith from the Forty Hadith of Nawawi on divine decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith of the lifted pens serves as a proof for the Islamic doctrine of divine decree (qadar).

Core Idea
All benefit and harm are by Allah's decree; the pens have been lifted and pages dried.

This lesson centers on a powerful hadith from the Forty Hadith of Nawawi, often cited by scholars of creed to affirm the reality of divine decree. The Prophet ﷺ teaches a young Ibn Abbas that no one can benefit or harm him except by what Allah has written. This passage grounds the believer's trust in Allah's preordainment while preserving the call to action.

Guided Path
1
Read the creedal statement
Begin with the opening line of the source: 'We believe that what missed the servant was not to hit him and what hit him was not to miss him.' Reflect on its meaning.
This statement summarizes the belief in qadar.
2
Study the hadith text
Read the complete hadith from Ibn Abbas, paying attention to the key phrases: 'preserve Allah, He will preserve you' and 'the pens have been lifted and the pages have dried.'
The hadith is from al-Tirmidhi and is graded hasan sahih.
3
Understand the proof for qadar
The hadith demonstrates that all outcomes, whether benefit or harm, are by Allah's prior writing. This is a direct proof for the doctrine of divine decree.
4
Apply the lesson
Reflect on how this hadith encourages reliance on Allah while still fulfilling religious obligations. It does not negate human effort but orients it within divine sovereignty.
The common misunderstanding is that it negates effort; it actually teaches tawakkul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) نؤمن أن (ما أخطأ العبد لم يكن ليصيبه وما أصابه لم يكن ليخطئه)؛ ففي الأربعين النووية: عن أبي العباس عبدالله بن عباس قال: كنتُ خلف النبي فقال: «يَا غُلَامُ إِنِّي أُعَلِّمُكَ كَلِمَاتٍ احْفَظِ اللَّهَ يَحْفَظْكَ احْفَظِ اللَّهَ تَجِدْهُ تُجَاهَكَ إِذَا سَأَلْتَ فَاسْأَلِ اللَّهَ وَإِذَا اسْتَعَنْتَ فَاسْتَعِنْ بِاللَّهِ وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ الْأُمَّةَ لَوِ اجْتَمَعَتْ عَلَى أَنْ يَنْفَعُوكَ بِشَيْءٍ لَمْ يَنْفَعُوكَ إِلَّا بِشَيْءٍ قَدْ كَتَبَهُ اللَّهُ لَكَ وَإِنِ اجْتَمَعُوا عَلَى أَنْ يَضُرُّوكَ بِشَيْءٍ لَمْ يَضُرُّوكَ إِلَّا بِشَيْءٍ قَدْ كَتَبَهُ اللهُ عَلَيكَ رُفِعَتِ الأَقْلَامُ وَجَفَّتِ الصُّحُفُ) رواه الترمذي، وقال: حسن صحيح (۱) (۲) (و) الواجب على العبد أن يعلم أن الله تعالى (قد سبق علمه في كل شيء
(And) we believe that (what missed the servant was not to hit him and what hit him was not to miss him). So in the Forty Hadith of Nawawi: from Abu al-‘Abbas ‘Abdullah ibn ‘Abbas, he said: I was behind the Prophet ﷺ and he said: 'O boy, I teach you words: preserve Allah, He will preserve you; preserve Allah, you will find Him before you. When you ask, ask Allah; when you seek help, seek help from Allah. Know that if the whole nation gathered to benefit you with something, they would not benefit you except with something Allah has written for you; and if they gathered to harm you with something, they would not harm you except with something Allah has written against you. The pens have been lifted and the pages have dried.' Reported by al-Tirmidhi, who said: hasan sahih. (1) (2) (And) it is obligatory upon the servant to know that Allah, Exalted is He, (has preceded in His knowledge in every thing...)
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the Tahawiyyah creed about divine decree. The author reaffirms the creedal statement and then provides a hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari? Actually from Tirmidhi, from the famous hadith of Ibn Abbas known from the Forty Hadith of Nawawi. The hadith emphasizes that all benefit and harm are by Allah's pre-writing, and that the pens of destiny have been lifted and the pages dried, meaning that everything is already decreed. The author then concludes with the obligation for the servant to know that Allah's knowledge preceded all things. This hadith serves as a strong proof for predestination and trust in Allah.

Key Terms
رفعت الأقلام
جفت الصحف
الأربعين النووية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the hadith negates human effort and free will, leading to fatalism.
Correction: The hadith actually encourages reliance on Allah (tawakkul) while still commanding action ('preserve Allah'). It affirms that outcomes are by Allah's decree, but humans are still responsible for their choices and actions.

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet ﷺ tell Ibn Abbas about the ability of people to benefit or harm him?
A) They can if they all agree
B) They cannot except by what Allah has written
C) They can only harm but not benefit
D) It depends on one's actions

Key Takeaway
The hadith of the lifted pens is a foundational proof in Sunni creed that all benefit and harm are by Allah's decree, yet it calls believers to action and trust in Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a harm—an illness, a loss, a disappointment—do you truly believe that no one could have prevented it except by Allah's decree? Or is there a hidden trust in means and people? Reflect on a recent affliction: where did your heart turn first? Is there a gap between your belief and your reaction?
?
You recite this hadith: 'If the whole nation gathered to benefit you, they would benefit you only with what Allah has written.' Does your heart rest in this, or are you still anxiously seeking benefit from people? Commit to one action today where you will turn to Allah alone for a need you previously relied on others for.
?
The pens are lifted and pages dried—there is no changing what has been decreed. Do you still hold regret over past misfortunes, as if they could have been different? What would it mean for you to accept that what happened was exactly what Allah wrote, and to find peace in that?

The Unalterable Decree: What Misses and Hits
Creedal statement on decree with supporting hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Tahawiyyah's statement that what misses the servant could not have hit him, and what hits him could not have missed him, and the prophetic proof for this belief.

Core Idea
Every occurrence is predetermined; no one can change Allah's decree.

The Tahawiyyah begins with a profound statement about divine decree: everything that happens to a person is exactly what was destined. This lesson examines this statement and the powerful hadith from the Prophet ﷺ that reinforces it.

Guided Path
1
Read the creedal statement
Read the first part of the passage carefully. Notice how it asserts that no mistake can hit what was destined to miss, and vice versa.
This is a direct statement of belief in predestination.
2
Study the hadith
Read the hadith from Ibn Abbas. Note how the Prophet teaches that the entire community cannot benefit or harm you except by Allah's written decree.
The hadith ends with 'the pens have been lifted, the pages have dried'—emphasizing finality.
3
Reflect on the connection
Consider how the hadith serves as a proof for the creedal statement. Why is this hadith particularly powerful?

وَمَا أَخْطَأَ العَبْدَ لَمْ يَكُنْ لِيُصِيبَهُ وَمَا أَصَابَهُ لَمْ يَكُنْ لِيُخْطِئَهُ، وَعَلَى العَبْدِ أَنْ يَعْلَمَ أَنَّ اللهَ قَدْ سَبَقَ عِلْمُهُ فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ كَائِنِ مِنْ خَلْقِهِ وَقَدَّرَ ذَلِكَ بِمَشِيئَتِهِ تَقْدِيرًا مُحْكَما مُبْرَمًا لَيْسَ فِيهِ نَاقِضُ وَلَا مُعَقِّبٌ وَلَا مُزِيلٌ وَلَا مُغَيَّرٌ وَلَا مُحَوِّلٌ وَلَا زَائِدٌ وَلَا نَاقِصٌ مِنْ خَلْقِهِ فِي سَمَوَاتِهِ وَأَرْضِهِ، وَذَلِكَ مِنْ عَقْدِ الإِيمَانِ وَأُصُولِ الْمَعْرِفَةِ والاعتراف بِتَوْحِيدِ اللهِ وَرُبُوبِيَّتِهِ كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى فِي كِتَابِهِ العَزِيزِ: ﴿وَخَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَقَدَّرَهُ تَقْدِيرًا ﴾ [سورة الفرقان آية: (٢) وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿ وَكَانَ أَمْرُ اللَّهِ قَدَرًا مقدورًا ﴾ [سورة الأحزاب آية: ۳۸]؛ فَوَيْلٌ لِمَنْ صَارَ لَهُ اللَّهُ فِي القَدَرِ خَصِيمًا وَأَحْضَرَ لِلنَّظَرِ فِيهِ قَلْبًا سَقِيمًا؛ لَقَدِ الْتَمَسَ بِوَهْمِهِ فِي مَحْضِ الغَيبِ سِرًّا كَتِيمًا وَعَادَ بِمَا قَالَ فِيهِ آثِمًا.
(و) نؤمن أن (ما أخطأ العبد لم يكن ليصيبه وما أصابه لم يكن ليخطئه)؛ ففي الأربعين النووية: عن أبي العباس عبدالله بن عباس قال: كنتُ خلف النبي فقال: «يَا غُلَامُ إِنِّي أُعَلِّمُكَ كَلِمَاتٍ احْفَظِ اللَّهَ يَحْفَظْكَ احْفَظِ اللَّهَ تَجِدْهُ تُجَاهَكَ إِذَا سَأَلْتَ فَاسْأَلِ اللَّهَ وَإِذَا اسْتَعَنْتَ فَاسْتَعِنْ بِاللَّهِ وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ الْأُمَّةَ لَوِ اجْتَمَعَتْ عَلَى أَنْ يَنْفَعُوكَ بِشَيْءٍ لَمْ يَنْفَعُوكَ إِلَّا بِشَيْءٍ قَدْ كَتَبَهُ اللَّهُ لَكَ وَإِنِ اجْتَمَعُوا عَلَى أَنْ يَضُرُّوكَ بِشَيْءٍ لَمْ يَضُرُّوكَ إِلَّا بِشَيْءٍ قَدْ كَتَبَهُ اللهُ عَلَيكَ رُفِعَتِ الأَقْلَامُ وَجَفَّتِ الصُّحُفُ) رواه الترمذي، وقال: حسن صحيح (۱) (۲) (و) الواجب على العبد أن يعلم أن الله تعالى (قد سبق علمه في كل شيء كائن من جميع خلقه وقدر ذلك ) وقضاه (بمشيئته ) وإرادته (تقديرا محكما مبرما)، وأنه ليس فيه ناقض ولا معقب ولا مزيل ولا مغير ولا محول ولا زائد ولا ناقص من جميع خلقه في سمواته وأرضه، وذلك من عقد الإيمان)؛ من إضافة الصفة إلى الموصوف؛ أي الإيمان المعقود عليه بالإيقان، (و) من أصول المعرفة) لأهل العرفان. (والاعتراف بالرفع عطفا على المصدر المتأول من "أن يعلم"؛ أي الواجب العلم والاعتراف بتوحيد الله تعالى بأنه هو الموجد للكائنات بأسرها من غير تأثير لدهر أو لنوء (۱) أو غيرها من الأسباب العادية؛ فإنها غير مؤثرة بطبعها وإنما المؤثر هو الله تعالى وحده عندها؛ ولذا سميت عادية، (وربوبيته) فيتصرف في ملكه بمشيئته على حسب ما سبق في علمه وحكمته كما قال تعالى في كتابه العزيز: ﴿وَخَلَقَ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ فَقَدْرَهُ، تَقْدِيرًا ﴾ [سورة الفرقان آية: ٢]، وقال تعالى: وَكَانَ أَمْرُ اللهِ قَدَرًا مقدورًا ) (سورة الأحزاب آية : ٣٨])؛ فهذا وغيره من الآيات الكثيرة إخبار منه تعالى بأنه الخالق لكل شيء والمقدر له؛ فمن لم يعترف بذلك فهو خصمه؛ فويل لمن صار له الله في القدر خصيصًا وأحضر للنظر فيه قلبا سقيما) وعقلا ذميا؛ فإنه (لقد التمس بوهمه في محض الغيب سرا كتيها وعاد بما قال فيه أناكًا أثيا). هو (۱) النوء: سقوط النجم في المغرب مع الفجر وطلوع آخر يقابله من ساعته في المشرق، وكانت العرب تُضيف الأمطار والرياح والحر والبرد إلى الساقط منها، وقيل: إلى الطالع منها، والجمع: أنواء.
And what missed the servant could not have hit him, and what hit him could not have missed him. And upon the servant is to know that Allah – exalted is He – His knowledge has preceded in everything that occurs from His creation, and He decreed that by His will, a firm and binding decree, in which there is no repudiator, no annuller, no remover, no changer, no transformer, no increase, no decrease from His creation in His heavens and His earth. And that is from the bond of faith and the foundations of knowledge and acknowledgment of the oneness of Allah and His lordship, as He said in His Mighty Book: {And He created everything and ordained it in due measure} [Surah al-Furqan, verse 2] and He said: {And the command of Allah is a decree determined} [Surah al-Ahzab, verse 38]. So woe to the one who makes Allah his opponent concerning the decree and brings for speculation about it a sick heart; he has sought with his illusion in the pure unseen a hidden secret, and he returns with what he says about it a sinner. (And) we believe that what missed the servant could not have hit him and what hit him could not have missed him; for in al-Arba'een al-Nawawiyyah: from Abu al-Abbas Abdullah ibn Abbas who said: I was behind the Prophet and he said: 'O boy, I will teach you words: Preserve Allah and He will preserve you. Preserve Allah and you will find Him before you. When you ask, ask of Allah, and when you seek help, seek help from Allah. And know that if the whole community gathered to benefit you with something, they would not benefit you except with something Allah has written for you; and if they gathered to harm you with something, they would not harm you except with something Allah has written upon you. The pens have been lifted and the pages have dried.' Reported by al-Tirmidhi and he said: hasan sahih. (1) (2) (And) the obligation upon the servant is to know that Allah – exalted is He – His knowledge has preceded in everything that occurs from all His creation and He decreed that and ordained it by His will and His will, a firm and binding decree, and that there is no repudiator in it, no annuller, no remover, no changer, no transformer, no increase, no decrease from all His creation in His heavens and His earth. And that is from the bond of faith – by adding the attribute to the described, i.e., faith contracted upon certainty – and from the foundations of knowledge for the people of recognition. And acknowledgment – in the accusative case, coordinated with the verbal noun derived from 'to know' – i.e., the obligation is knowledge and acknowledgment of the oneness of Allah – exalted is He – that He is the creator of all existences without any effect from time or from a star's setting or other customary causes; for they are not effective by their nature, but the effective agent is Allah alone alongside them; therefore they are called customary. And His lordship, so He disposes in His dominion by His will according to what has preceded in His knowledge and wisdom, as He said in His Mighty Book: {And He created everything and ordained it in due measure} [Surah al-Furqan, verse 2] and He said: {And the command of Allah is a decree determined} [Surah al-Ahzab, verse 38]; so this and other numerous verses are information from Him – exalted is He – that He is the creator of everything and the ordainer of it; so whoever does not acknowledge that, he is His opponent. So woe to the one for whom Allah becomes an opponent concerning the decree and who brings for speculation about it a sick heart and a blameworthy mind; for he has sought with his illusion in the pure unseen a hidden secret and he returns with what he says about it a sinner. He (1) al-naw' (star-setting) is the setting of a star in the west at dawn and the rising of another opposite it at the same moment in the east, and the Arabs used to attribute rains, winds, heat and cold to the one that set, and it is said to the one that rose; the plural is anwa'.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on two interconnected creedal statements from the Tahawiyyah concerning divine decree (qadar). The author begins by quoting the Tahawiyyah text: 'And what missed the servant could not have hit him, and what hit him could not have missed him.' This establishes that every occurrence—whether beneficial or harmful—is predetermined. The text then states the obligation for the servant to know that Allah's knowledge has preceded all things, and that He decreed them with His will in a firm and binding decree that has no repudiator, annuller, remover, changer, transformer, increase, or decrease. This decree is described as 'muhkaman mubraman' (firm and binding), emphasizing its unalterability. The author then explains that this belief is part of the 'bond of faith' and the 'foundations of knowledge,' and leads to acknowledgment of Allah's tawhid (oneness) and rububiyyah (lordship). Two Quranic verses are cited: Surah al-Furqan 2 and Surah al-Ahzab 38, which affirm that Allah creates and ordains everything.

After the initial quote, the commentator reasserts the belief (numinu) in the first statement and supports it with a hadith from Ibn Abbas (the famous 'Preserve Allah' hadith), which explicitly states that no one can benefit or harm you except by Allah's decree, and that the pens have been lifted and the pages have dried. This hadith reinforces the certainty and finality of the decree.

The commentator then turns to the second part of the Tahawiyyah text regarding the obligation to know that Allah's knowledge preceded all creation and that He decreed with His will a firm and binding decree. He provides a detailed explanation: the phrase 'from the bond of faith' means faith that is contracted and bound with certainty. 'From the foundations of knowledge' refers to the knowledge of the people of gnosis (ahl al-'irfan). The acknowledgment of tawhid and rububiyyah is explained as the belief that Allah is the sole creator of all existences, with no effect from time (dahr), the setting of stars (naw'), or other customary causes. Customary causes are not effective by their own nature; rather, Allah is the only true agent, and these causes are merely occasions. This refutes any belief in independent natural causality. The commentator then repeats the Quranic verses and warns against disputing qadar: whoever does not acknowledge Allah's exclusive creation and ordainment makes himself Allah's opponent. The passage ends with a severe warning to those who argue about qadar with a sick heart and blameworthy mind, likening their search to seeking an impossible hidden secret, and they return as sinners. A lexical note on 'naw' (star-setting) is appended, explaining the pre-Islamic Arab practice of attributing weather phenomena to stars, which is implicitly rejected as a false cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People can independently benefit or harm you regardless of Allah's will.
Correction: The hadith teaches that no one can benefit or harm you except by Allah's decree.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in this passage, what does the Prophet teach the young boy about the community's ability to benefit or harm him?
A) The community can benefit him if they cooperate.
B) The community can harm him if they all agree.
C) The community cannot benefit or harm him except by what Allah has written.
D) The community can override Allah's decree if they gather.

Key Takeaway
The decree is unchangeable; the Prophet's instruction to the young boy reinforces that all outcomes are from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When a trial strikes you, do you truly believe that it could not have missed you? Or does your heart secretly wish it had been different, as if you know better than Allah's decree? How will you train yourself this week to say and feel 'قدر الله وما شاء فعل' with full certainty?
?
You have been given the hadith: 'احفظ الله يحفظك'—but are you actually preserving Allah's commands in your daily life? Or do you neglect them, hoping that your actions don't really affect His protection over you? Name one command you will start preserving today as a direct response to this lesson.
?
The lesson warns of a 'sick heart' that argues with Allah over the decree. Where in your life do you find yourself questioning or resenting what Allah has decreed—over your past, your provision, or your future? What would it cost you to surrender that argument right now, and will you do it?

Divine Decree
intermediate
6 min
The Firm Decree and Its Theological Foundations
Detailed explanation of the obligation to believe in the firm decree and its implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation to know Allah's foreknowledge and the firm decree, and how this belief is integral to tawhid and rububiyyah.

Core Idea
Belief in the unalterable decree is part of faith and acknowledges Allah as the sole creator and ordainer.

The Tahawiyyah continues by emphasizing the obligation to know that Allah's knowledge preceded all creation and that He decreed everything with His will in a firm and binding manner. This lesson explores the explanation of this decree as part of the bond of faith, the foundations of knowledge, and the acknowledgment of Allah's oneness and lordship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the obligation
Read the second part of the text carefully. Note the repeated emphasis on the firmness of the decree and the list of things it is immune from (no repudiator, annuller, etc.).
The phrase 'muhkaman mubraman' is key.
2
Understand its theological context
The passage explains that this belief is from the 'bond of faith' and 'foundations of knowledge'. Why is qadar so central to faith?
Think about tawhid and rububiyyah.
3
Reflect on the warning
Read the warning against disputing qadar. What does it mean to make Allah an opponent in qadar?
The passage says such a person returns as a sinner.
