وَمَا أَخْطَأَ العَبْدَ لَمْ يَكُنْ لِيُصِيبَهُ وَمَا أَصَابَهُ لَمْ يَكُنْ لِيُخْطِئَهُ، وَعَلَى العَبْدِ أَنْ يَعْلَمَ أَنَّ اللهَ قَدْ سَبَقَ عِلْمُهُ فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ كَائِنِ مِنْ خَلْقِهِ وَقَدَّرَ ذَلِكَ بِمَشِيئَتِهِ تَقْدِيرًا مُحْكَما مُبْرَمًا لَيْسَ فِيهِ نَاقِضُ وَلَا مُعَقِّبٌ وَلَا مُزِيلٌ وَلَا مُغَيَّرٌ وَلَا مُحَوِّلٌ وَلَا زَائِدٌ وَلَا نَاقِصٌ مِنْ خَلْقِهِ فِي سَمَوَاتِهِ وَأَرْضِهِ، وَذَلِكَ مِنْ عَقْدِ الإِيمَانِ وَأُصُولِ الْمَعْرِفَةِ والاعتراف بِتَوْحِيدِ اللهِ وَرُبُوبِيَّتِهِ كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى فِي كِتَابِهِ العَزِيزِ: ﴿وَخَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَقَدَّرَهُ تَقْدِيرًا ﴾ [سورة الفرقان آية: (٢) وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿ وَكَانَ أَمْرُ اللَّهِ قَدَرًا مقدورًا ﴾ [سورة الأحزاب آية: ۳۸]؛ فَوَيْلٌ لِمَنْ صَارَ لَهُ اللَّهُ فِي القَدَرِ خَصِيمًا وَأَحْضَرَ لِلنَّظَرِ فِيهِ قَلْبًا سَقِيمًا؛ لَقَدِ الْتَمَسَ بِوَهْمِهِ فِي مَحْضِ الغَيبِ سِرًّا كَتِيمًا وَعَادَ بِمَا قَالَ فِيهِ آثِمًا.
(و) نؤمن أن (ما أخطأ العبد لم يكن ليصيبه وما أصابه لم يكن ليخطئه)؛ ففي الأربعين النووية: عن أبي العباس عبدالله بن عباس قال: كنتُ خلف النبي فقال: «يَا غُلَامُ إِنِّي أُعَلِّمُكَ كَلِمَاتٍ احْفَظِ اللَّهَ يَحْفَظْكَ احْفَظِ اللَّهَ تَجِدْهُ تُجَاهَكَ إِذَا سَأَلْتَ فَاسْأَلِ اللَّهَ وَإِذَا اسْتَعَنْتَ فَاسْتَعِنْ بِاللَّهِ وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ الْأُمَّةَ لَوِ اجْتَمَعَتْ عَلَى أَنْ يَنْفَعُوكَ بِشَيْءٍ لَمْ يَنْفَعُوكَ إِلَّا بِشَيْءٍ قَدْ كَتَبَهُ اللَّهُ لَكَ وَإِنِ اجْتَمَعُوا عَلَى أَنْ يَضُرُّوكَ بِشَيْءٍ لَمْ يَضُرُّوكَ إِلَّا بِشَيْءٍ قَدْ كَتَبَهُ اللهُ عَلَيكَ رُفِعَتِ الأَقْلَامُ وَجَفَّتِ الصُّحُفُ) رواه الترمذي، وقال: حسن صحيح (۱) (۲) (و) الواجب على العبد أن يعلم أن الله تعالى (قد سبق علمه في كل شيء كائن من جميع خلقه وقدر ذلك ) وقضاه (بمشيئته ) وإرادته (تقديرا محكما مبرما)، وأنه ليس فيه ناقض ولا معقب ولا مزيل ولا مغير ولا محول ولا زائد ولا ناقص من جميع خلقه في سمواته وأرضه، وذلك من عقد الإيمان)؛ من إضافة الصفة إلى الموصوف؛ أي الإيمان المعقود عليه بالإيقان، (و) من أصول المعرفة) لأهل العرفان. (والاعتراف بالرفع عطفا على المصدر المتأول من "أن يعلم"؛ أي الواجب العلم والاعتراف بتوحيد الله تعالى بأنه هو الموجد للكائنات بأسرها من غير تأثير لدهر أو لنوء (۱) أو غيرها من الأسباب العادية؛ فإنها غير مؤثرة بطبعها وإنما المؤثر هو الله تعالى وحده عندها؛ ولذا سميت عادية، (وربوبيته) فيتصرف في ملكه بمشيئته على حسب ما سبق في علمه وحكمته كما قال تعالى في كتابه العزيز: ﴿وَخَلَقَ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ فَقَدْرَهُ، تَقْدِيرًا ﴾ [سورة الفرقان آية: ٢]، وقال تعالى: وَكَانَ أَمْرُ اللهِ قَدَرًا مقدورًا ) (سورة الأحزاب آية : ٣٨])؛ فهذا وغيره من الآيات الكثيرة إخبار منه تعالى بأنه الخالق لكل شيء والمقدر له؛ فمن لم يعترف بذلك فهو خصمه؛ فويل لمن صار له الله في القدر خصيصًا وأحضر للنظر فيه قلبا سقيما) وعقلا ذميا؛ فإنه (لقد التمس بوهمه في محض الغيب سرا كتيها وعاد بما قال فيه أناكًا أثيا). هو (۱) النوء: سقوط النجم في المغرب مع الفجر وطلوع آخر يقابله من ساعته في المشرق، وكانت العرب تُضيف الأمطار والرياح والحر والبرد إلى الساقط منها، وقيل: إلى الطالع منها، والجمع: أنواء.
And what missed the servant could not have hit him, and what hit him could not have missed him. And upon the servant is to know that Allah – exalted is He – His knowledge has preceded in everything that occurs from His creation, and He decreed that by His will, a firm and binding decree, in which there is no repudiator, no annuller, no remover, no changer, no transformer, no increase, no decrease from His creation in His heavens and His earth. And that is from the bond of faith and the foundations of knowledge and acknowledgment of the oneness of Allah and His lordship, as He said in His Mighty Book: {And He created everything and ordained it in due measure} [Surah al-Furqan, verse 2] and He said: {And the command of Allah is a decree determined} [Surah al-Ahzab, verse 38]. So woe to the one who makes Allah his opponent concerning the decree and brings for speculation about it a sick heart; he has sought with his illusion in the pure unseen a hidden secret, and he returns with what he says about it a sinner. (And) we believe that what missed the servant could not have hit him and what hit him could not have missed him; for in al-Arba'een al-Nawawiyyah: from Abu al-Abbas Abdullah ibn Abbas who said: I was behind the Prophet and he said: 'O boy, I will teach you words: Preserve Allah and He will preserve you. Preserve Allah and you will find Him before you. When you ask, ask of Allah, and when you seek help, seek help from Allah. And know that if the whole community gathered to benefit you with something, they would not benefit you except with something Allah has written for you; and if they gathered to harm you with something, they would not harm you except with something Allah has written upon you. The pens have been lifted and the pages have dried.' Reported by al-Tirmidhi and he said: hasan sahih. (1) (2) (And) the obligation upon the servant is to know that Allah – exalted is He – His knowledge has preceded in everything that occurs from all His creation and He decreed that and ordained it by His will and His will, a firm and binding decree, and that there is no repudiator in it, no annuller, no remover, no changer, no transformer, no increase, no decrease from all His creation in His heavens and His earth. And that is from the bond of faith – by adding the attribute to the described, i.e., faith contracted upon certainty – and from the foundations of knowledge for the people of recognition. And acknowledgment – in the accusative case, coordinated with the verbal noun derived from 'to know' – i.e., the obligation is knowledge and acknowledgment of the oneness of Allah – exalted is He – that He is the creator of all existences without any effect from time or from a star's setting or other customary causes; for they are not effective by their nature, but the effective agent is Allah alone alongside them; therefore they are called customary. And His lordship, so He disposes in His dominion by His will according to what has preceded in His knowledge and wisdom, as He said in His Mighty Book: {And He created everything and ordained it in due measure} [Surah al-Furqan, verse 2] and He said: {And the command of Allah is a decree determined} [Surah al-Ahzab, verse 38]; so this and other numerous verses are information from Him – exalted is He – that He is the creator of everything and the ordainer of it; so whoever does not acknowledge that, he is His opponent. So woe to the one for whom Allah becomes an opponent concerning the decree and who brings for speculation about it a sick heart and a blameworthy mind; for he has sought with his illusion in the pure unseen a hidden secret and he returns with what he says about it a sinner. He (1) al-naw' (star-setting) is the setting of a star in the west at dawn and the rising of another opposite it at the same moment in the east, and the Arabs used to attribute rains, winds, heat and cold to the one that set, and it is said to the one that rose; the plural is anwa'.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on two interconnected creedal statements from the Tahawiyyah concerning divine decree (qadar). The author begins by quoting the Tahawiyyah text: 'And what missed the servant could not have hit him, and what hit him could not have missed him.' This establishes that every occurrence—whether beneficial or harmful—is predetermined. The text then states the obligation for the servant to know that Allah's knowledge has preceded all things, and that He decreed them with His will in a firm and binding decree that has no repudiator, annuller, remover, changer, transformer, increase, or decrease. This decree is described as 'muhkaman mubraman' (firm and binding), emphasizing its unalterability. The author then explains that this belief is part of the 'bond of faith' and the 'foundations of knowledge,' and leads to acknowledgment of Allah's tawhid (oneness) and rububiyyah (lordship). Two Quranic verses are cited: Surah al-Furqan 2 and Surah al-Ahzab 38, which affirm that Allah creates and ordains everything.

After the initial quote, the commentator reasserts the belief (numinu) in the first statement and supports it with a hadith from Ibn Abbas (the famous 'Preserve Allah' hadith), which explicitly states that no one can benefit or harm you except by Allah's decree, and that the pens have been lifted and the pages have dried. This hadith reinforces the certainty and finality of the decree.

The commentator then turns to the second part of the Tahawiyyah text regarding the obligation to know that Allah's knowledge preceded all creation and that He decreed with His will a firm and binding decree. He provides a detailed explanation: the phrase 'from the bond of faith' means faith that is contracted and bound with certainty. 'From the foundations of knowledge' refers to the knowledge of the people of gnosis (ahl al-'irfan). The acknowledgment of tawhid and rububiyyah is explained as the belief that Allah is the sole creator of all existences, with no effect from time (dahr), the setting of stars (naw'), or other customary causes. Customary causes are not effective by their own nature; rather, Allah is the only true agent, and these causes are merely occasions. This refutes any belief in independent natural causality. The commentator then repeats the Quranic verses and warns against disputing qadar: whoever does not acknowledge Allah's exclusive creation and ordainment makes himself Allah's opponent. The passage ends with a severe warning to those who argue about qadar with a sick heart and blameworthy mind, likening their search to seeking an impossible hidden secret, and they return as sinners. A lexical note on 'naw' (star-setting) is appended, explaining the pre-Islamic Arab practice of attributing weather phenomena to stars, which is implicitly rejected as a false cause.

Key Terms
قدر
مشيئة
علم
إيمان
توحيد
ربوبية
أسباب عادية
تقدير مبرم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Belief in qadar negates the use of means and effort; everything is predetermined so actions are meaningless.
Correction: The passage clarifies that customary causes (al-asbāb al-‘ādī) are not effective by themselves; Allah is the true agent, but He creates effects through these means. So using means is part of the decree.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are customary causes called 'ādī (customary)?
A) Because they are recommended by custom.
B) Because they are not effective by nature; Allah alone is the true agent.
C) Because they are prescribed in the Quran.
D) Because they are superstitious.

Key Takeaway
Belief in the firm decree is an integral part of faith and tawhid; it requires acknowledging Allah as the sole creator and ordainer, and rejecting any independent causes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial, is your first reaction to attribute it to a natural cause (like your own mistake, someone else's action, or 'bad luck')? How does this passage demand you reorient your heart towards Allah's sole effect?
?
Have you ever felt anger or resentment towards a situation, secretly believing that some other force or person could have changed it? How does the teaching of the firm decree with no annuller or changer challenge that assumption?
?
Do you truly believe that Allah's decree is unalterable, or is there a part of you that thinks you can escape it by your own planning or effort? Reflect on a specific instance in your life: did that effort come to pass, or was it ultimately Allah's decree that prevailed?

The Firmness of Allah's Decree in Faith
Sanusi describes the unchangeable nature of Allah's decree and its place in faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that everything in creation is decreed by Allah with a firm, unchangeable decree, and that affirming this is a core part of faith.

Core Idea
Allah's decree is absolute, unchangeable, and essential to faith.

The passage opens by declaring that every existing thing from Allah's creation is decreed and ordained by His will, a decree that is firm and decisive with no nullifier or revoker. This affirmation is presented not as a mere theological opinion, but as the very contract of faith – a binding belief rooted in certainty. Before we explore the implications for causation, we must first grasp the immutability of the divine decree itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the first part of the source passage (Arabic and translation) focusing on the description of the decree and its attributes. Notice the key phrases.
Pay attention to the list of negations: no nullifier, revoker, etc.
2
Identify the key attributes of the decree
Identify the phrase 'تقديرا محكما مبرما' and the list of what the decree lacks. Understand that these negate any possibility of change or interference.
The decree is described as firm (محكما) and decisive (مبرما).
3
Connect to faith
Understand how the commentator anchors this belief in 'عقد الإيمان' (contract of faith) and 'أصول المعرفة' (principles of knowledge). Ask yourself: why is this belief so fundamental?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كائن من جميع خلقه وقدر ذلك وقضاه بمشيئته وإرادته تقديرا محكما مبرما، وأنه ليس فيه ناقض ولا معقب ولا مزيل ولا مغير ولا محول ولا زائد ولا ناقص من جميع خلقه في سمواته وأرضه، وذلك من عقد الإيمان؛ من إضافة الصفة إلى الموصوف؛ أي الإيمان المعقود عليه بالإيقان، ومن أصول المعرفة لأهل العرفان. والاعتراف بالرفع عطفا على المصدر المتأول من "أن يعلم"؛ أي الواجب العلم والاعتراف بتوحيد الله تعالى بأنه هو الموجد للكائنات بأسرها من غير تأثير لدهر أو لنوء أو غيرها من الأسباب العادية؛ فإنها غير مؤثرة بطبعها وإنما المؤثر هو الله تعالى وحده عندها؛ ولذا سميت عادية، وربوبيته فيتصرف في ملكه بمشيئته على حسب ما سبق في علمه وحكمته كما قال تعالى في كتابه العزيز: (وَخَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَقَدَّرَهُ تَقْدِيرًا) [سورة الفرقان آية: ٢]، وقال تعالى: (وَكَانَ أَمْرُ اللهِ قَدَرًا مَقْدُورًا) [سورة الأحزاب آية: ٣٨]؛ فهذا وغيره من الآيات الكثيرة إخبار منه تعالى بأنه الخالق لكل شيء والمقدر له؛ فمن لم يعترف بذلك فهو خصمه؛ فويل لمن صار له الله في القدر خصيما وأحضر للنظر فيه قلبا سقيما وعقلا ذميما؛ فإنه لقد التمس بوهمه في محض الغيب سرا كتيما وعاد بما قال فيه إناكا أثيما.
Everything that exists from all His creation and He decreed that and ordained it with His will and desire, a firm and decisive decree, and that there is in it no nullifier, no revoker, no remover, no changer, no alterer, no increaser, no decreaser from all His creation in His heavens and His earth. That is from the contract of faith – by adding the attribute to the described; i.e. faith contracted upon with certainty – and from the principles of knowledge for the people of insight. And the acknowledgment – raised as a conjunction to the verbal noun from 'that He knows' – i.e. obligatory knowledge and acknowledgment of the tawhid of Allah Most High, that He is the originator of all beings entirely, without any effect from time or from a lunar mansion or other customary causes; for they are not effective by their nature, rather the only effective agent is Allah Most High alone with them; hence they are called customary. And His lordship, so He disposes in His kingdom by His will according to what preceded in His knowledge and wisdom, as He said in His noble Book: 'And He created everything and determined it with determination' (Quran 25:2), and He said: 'And the command of Allah is a decree determined' (Quran 33:38). So this and other numerous verses are information from Him Most High that He is the Creator of everything and the Determiner for it. So whoever does not acknowledge that is His adversary; so woe to him for whom Allah becomes in qadar an adversary, and who brings for considering it a sick heart and a blameworthy intellect; for he sought by his illusion in the pure unseen a hidden secret, and he returned with what he said therein a sinful liar.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Tahawiyyah statement regarding qadar. It begins by affirming that everything existing from all of Allah's creation is decreed and ordained by His will and desire, a decree that is firm and decisive with no nullifier, revoker, remover, changer, alterer, increaser, or decreaser in all of creation in the heavens and earth. This affirmation is part of the 'contract of faith' – a binding belief rooted in certainty – and is among the fundamental principles of knowledge for the people of true insight. The commentator then explains the obligation of knowledge and acknowledgment of Allah's tawhid, specifically that He alone is the originator of all beings without any influence from time, lunar mansions (as the pre-Islamic Arabs believed), or other customary causes. These causes are not effective by their own nature; rather, Allah alone is the true agent at the time of their occurrence, which is why they are called 'customary' (not essential). This applies to Allah's lordship, as He disposes of His kingdom by His will according to His prior knowledge and wisdom. The commentator supports this with two Quranic verses: 'And He created everything and determined it with determination' (25:2) and 'And the command of Allah is a decree determined' (33:38). These and many other verses inform that Allah is the Creator and Determiner of everything. Consequently, anyone who fails to acknowledge this becomes an adversary of Allah. The passage concludes with a severe warning: woe to the one for whom Allah becomes an adversary in the matter of qadar, who brings a sick heart and a blameworthy intellect to ponder it, for such a person seeks by his illusion a hidden secret in the unseen, only to end up returning with a sinful lie. This warns against delving into qadar with flawed reasoning.

Key Terms
القدر (al-qadar)
المشيئة (al-mashi'a)
الإرادة (al-irada)
التقدير (al-taqdir)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah's decree can be changed or revoked by external factors such as human actions or prayers.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that the decree has no nullifier, revoker, remover, etc., indicating that it is immutable and cannot be altered.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a quality of Allah's decree?
A) Firm
B) Decisive
C) Changeable
D) Ordained by His will

Key Takeaway
Allah's decree encompasses all creation and is absolutely firm and unchanging, forming a core pillar of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's decree is absolutely unchangeable, then where in your life do you still act as if your choices can overturn what He has written? What is the root of that contradiction?
?
The source calls this belief a 'contract of faith.' Have you ever truly felt bound by this contract? When does your heart deny it?
?
Which of your anxieties stems from forgetting that there is 'no increaser or decreaser' in Allah's decree? What would change if you lived that truth today?

Allah's Sole Agency and Warning against Disputing Qadar
Commentator explains tawhid in action, rejecting independent causes and warning against disputing qadar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah alone is the true creator and agent behind all things, that customary causes are not independent, and that disputing qadar leads to grave consequences.

Core Idea
Only Allah creates; customary causes are mere occasions.

The second part of the passage shifts from describing the decree to explaining its implications for causation. It affirms that Allah is the originator of all beings, without any influence from time or natural phenomena. These are only 'customary causes' – Allah alone is the effective agent. This understanding is reinforced by Quranic verses, and the passage ends with a stern warning against those who argue about qadar with a corrupted heart and intellect.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the doctrine of causation
Read how the passage negates any effect from time or lunar mansions and identifies Allah as the only true agent. Note the term 'الأسباب العادية' and its explanation.
The passage says these causes are not effective by nature; only Allah is effective.
2
Understand the Quranic evidence
The two verses cited – 25:2 and 33:38 – serve as proof for Allah's sole creation and determination. Read them and see how they support the argument.
3
Heed the warning
Read the concluding warning about becoming an adversary of Allah by denying or disputing this truth. Notice the description of a person who seeks a hidden secret in vain and ends up lying.
The warning is severe: 'woe to him for whom Allah becomes in qadar an adversary.'

Divine Decree

Belief in Divine Decree: Its Nature and Proofs
Commentary on the nature and inevitability of divine decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic belief in divine decree, including that whatever Allah decrees must occur and that both good and evil are from Allah.

Core Idea
Whatever Allah decrees must happen; whatever He does not decree can never occur.

The sixth pillar of iman is belief in divine decree (qadar). The matn affirms that both good and evil, sweet and bitter, come from Allah. The commentator clarifies that everything Allah decreed in His eternity is inevitable, and supports this with three Quranic verses. Let's explore this foundational belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Focus on the overall meaning before diving into details.
Notice the phrase 'good and its evil, its sweet and its bitter'—this covers all aspects of qadar.
2
Understand the nature of divine decree
The commentator states that whatever Allah decrees in His eternity must occur, and what He does not decree is impossible. Reflect on the absolute scope of Allah's will.
This includes both good and evil, decreed before creation.
3
Examine the Quranic proofs
Three verses are cited: 'Allah is the Creator of everything,' 'Allah created you and what you do,' and 'We have created everything with a measure.' Each affirms Allah's complete sovereignty over creation.
These verses collectively show that even human actions are created by Allah.
4
Address the common misunderstanding
Some think evil cannot be from Allah. The text clarifies that both good and evil are from Him, but this does not imply injustice—Allah's wisdom is perfect.
The hadith reference ('al-khabar') at the end points to further proof from the Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْقَدَرِ خَيْرِهِ وَشَرِّهِ وَحُلْوِهِ وَمُرِّهِ مِنَ الله تَعَالَى)؛ أي بأن جميع ما قدر الله تعالى في أزليته لابد من وقوعه وما لم يقدره يستحيل وقوعه، وبأنه تعالى قدر الخير والشر قبل خلق الخلق، وأن جميع الكائنات بقضائه وقدره وإرادته؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿اللهُ خَالِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ﴾ [سورة الأنعام آية: ١٠٢]، ﴿وَاللهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ﴾ [سورة الصافات آية: ٩٦]، ﴿إِنَّا كُلَّ شَيْءٍ خَلَقْنَاهُ بِقَدَرٍ﴾ [سورة القمر آية: ٤٩]... والخبر.
And divine decree, its good and its evil, its sweet and its bitter, from Allah Most High: i.e., that everything Allah decreed in His eternity must occur, and what He did not decree is impossible to occur, and that He Most High decreed good and evil before creating creation, and that all beings are by His decree, measure, and will; for His saying: {Allah is the Creator of everything} [Surah al-An'am, 102], {And Allah created you and what you do} [Surah al-Saffat, 96], {Indeed, We have created everything with a measure} [Surah al-Qamar, 49] ... and the hadith.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage explains the sixth pillar: belief in divine decree (qadar). The matn states that both good and evil, sweet and bitter, come from Allah. The commentator elaborates: what Allah decrees in His eternity is inevitable; what He does not decree can never occur. This includes both good and evil, established before creation. Then three Quranic proofs are cited: (1) Allah is the Creator of everything (al-An'am 102) — so all things, including acts of creatures, are created by Him. (2) Allah creates both you and your deeds (al-Saffat 96) — affirming creation of human actions. (3) Everything is created with a precise measure (al-Qamar 49) — confirming detailed predestination. The passage ends with a reference to a hadith (the word 'al-khabar' indicates a prophetic narration is quoted in the full text, though not fully given here).

Key Terms
قدر
أزلية
قضاء
إرادة
خالق كل شيء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Evil is not from Allah; He only creates good.
Correction: The text affirms that both good and evil, sweet and bitter, are from Allah. However, this does not attribute injustice to Allah; rather, His wisdom in creating evil is beyond human comprehension, and He is not to be questioned about what He does.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the relationship between Allah's decree and the occurrence of events?
A) Whatever Allah decrees must happen; whatever He does not decree cannot happen
B) Allah decrees only good; evil arises from human free will
C) Decree is allegorical and not to be taken literally
D) Decree applies only to major events, not to human actions

Key Takeaway
Belief in divine decree means accepting that everything that happens is by Allah's eternal decree, and that He is the Creator of all things, including human actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you truly believe that Allah created that action while you chose it? How does that change your repentance and reliance on Him?
?
Have you ever blamed Allah for a hardship, doubting His goodness? How does knowing that both good and evil are from His perfect decree transform your response to trials?
?
If every event in your life—down to your next breath—is precisely measured by Allah, why do you still worry about the future? What does that say about your trust in His decree?

The Reality of Divine Decree (Qadar)
Imam Maydani explains decree affirming everything is from Allah and citing Qur'anic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine of divine decree (qadar), that everything good and evil is from Allah, and the scriptural evidence for it.

Core Idea
Everything is by Allah's decree, including what we consider good or evil.

This lesson delves into one of the most profound and often misunderstood tenets of Islamic faith: divine decree, or qadar. Imam Maydani explains the creedal statement that all things—whether good or evil, sweet or bitter—are from Allah. He then provides the rational and scriptural basis for this belief, drawing on Quranic verses and prophetic traditions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic text and its translation to get the overall message.
Notice the strong opening statement.
2
Grasp the core meaning
Understand that the decree includes everything—good and evil—and that whatever Allah has decreed must happen.
3
Analyze the proofs
Examine the three Quranic verses and the hadith that support the doctrine. Each one reinforces Allah's absolute power over creation.
List them mentally.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this belief shapes a Muslim's worldview and response to events.
This is not fatalism but trust in Allah's wisdom.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقدر خيره وشره وحلوه ومره من الله تعالى)؛ أي بأن جميع ما قدر الله تعالى في أزليته لابد من وقوعه وما لم يقدره يستحيل وقوعه، وبأنه تعالى قدر الخير والشر قبل خلق الخلق، وأن جميع الكائنات بقضائه وقدره وإرادته؛ لقوله تعالى: خَلَقَ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ ﴾ [سورة الأنعام آية : ۱۰۱]، ﴿وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [سورة الصافات آية: ٩٦]، (إِنَّا كُلَّ شَيْءٍ خَلَقْتَهُ بِقَدْرِ) [سورة القمر آية: ٤٩]... والخبر كُلُّ شَيْءٍ بِقَدَرٍ حَتَّى العَجْرُ وَالكَيْسُ (١). والكل من شرح الأربعين لابن حجر على حديث جبريل (۲)
And the decree, its good and its evil, its sweet and its bitter, is from Allah. That is, everything that Allah has decreed in His eternity must occur, and what He has not decreed is impossible to occur. And He, exalted, decreed good and evil before creating creation, and all things happen by His judgment, predestination, and will. For His saying: 'He created everything' (Quran 6:101), 'And Allah created you and what you do' (Quran 37:96), 'Indeed, all things We created by predestination' (Quran 54:49) ... and the report: 'Everything is by decree, even incapacity and intelligence.' Commentary
This passage explains the creedal statement on divine decree. It begins by asserting that everything—good and evil, pleasant and painful—comes from Allah's decree. The author then gives the underlying principle: whatever Allah has decreed in His eternity necessarily happens; whatever He has not decreed cannot possibly happen. He further states that Allah decreed both good and evil before creating His creatures, and that all events occur by His judgment, decree, and will. Three Quranic verses are provided as evidence: (6:101) that Allah created everything, (37:96) that Allah created people and their actions, and (54:49) that everything is created by measure. The passage then quotes a prophetic report (khabar) that everything is by decree, including incapacity and intelligence. Finally, it notes that this entire discussion is drawn from Ibn Hajar's commentary on the hadith of Jibril in his work on the Forty Hadith.

Creation of Paradise and Hell and Their Inhabitants
Maydani explains that Allah created the inhabitants for Paradise and Hell and all deeds are predestined

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah created the inhabitants of Paradise and Hell based on His will, and that all actions are predestined.

Core Idea
Allah's decree is final; Paradise by His favor, Hell by His justice.

In this passage, Imam al-Maturidi (via Maydani) affirms the fundamental Islamic belief in predestination regarding the ultimate abodes of Paradise and Hell. He explains that Allah created both realms and their inhabitants, and that one's entry into Paradise is by divine favor, while entry into Hell is by divine justice. The passage also cites prophetic traditions that emphasize the finality of Allah's decree.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once without analysis. Let the author's own words establish the doctrine of predestination.
Notice the repeated emphasis on divine will and decree.
2
Identify the two foundations
The passage rests on two hadith: the divine hadith of the two handfuls and the hadith that the pens have dried. Find both and see how they support the doctrine.
The two handfuls represent the division of humanity into inhabitants of Paradise and Hell.
3
Understand favor vs justice
Paradise is entered by Allah's favor (fadl), Hell by His justice (adl). Reflect on why one is favor and the other justice.
This highlights that no one deserves Paradise; it is a gift.
4
Grasp the finality of decree
The phrase 'the pens have been lifted and the scrolls have dried' indicates that all destinies are finalized. Consider how this relates to human action.
Deeds are decreed, but people still choose within divine knowledge.

And indeed Allah Almighty created Paradise and Hell and created for them inhabitants; so whomever He wills, He admits to Paradise as a favor from Him, and whomever He wills among them, He admits to Hell as justice from Him. And everyone acts according to what has been decreed for him, and is bound to what he was created for. And good and evil are predestined for the servants. And we say: Indeed Allah Almighty created Paradise and Hell and created for them inhabitants, when He took two handfuls and said: 'These are for Paradise and I do not care, and these are for Hell and I do not care' – the sacred hadith. And each of them acts according to what has been decreed for him, where the pens have been lifted and the scrolls have dried as in the hadith, and he is destined by Allah's decree to what he was created for, and is the recipient of what was decreed for him. And good and evil are predestined for the servants, and this has preceded.

Commentary
This passage affirms the predestination of the inhabitants of Paradise and Hell. It begins with the creedal statement that Allah created both abodes and created their inhabitants. Entry into Paradise is by His favor, and into Hell by His justice. Everyone acts according to what has already been decreed and will end up in the place for which he was created. The commentary then elaborates with two hadith: the divine hadith of the two handfuls, where Allah declares that some are for Paradise and some for Hell, and the hadith that the Lord has finished with the servants, dividing them into two groups. The author explains that whoever is from the right handful enters Paradise by favor, and whoever is from the other enters Hell by justice. The deeds of each person have been written and the pens have dried, meaning their destiny is sealed. The passage concludes by restating that good and evil are predestined for the servants, as previously mentioned.

Imam Maydani presents a core Sunni creedal point: Allah created Paradise and Hell and predetermined who will inhabit them. Two Types of Istita'ah: Tawfiq and Capacity for Taklif
Maydani distinguishes two types of istita'ah and explains the meaning of 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will distinguish between the two types of capability—one that accompanies the act (tawfiq) and one that precedes it (health and means)—and understand how divine command relates to each.

Core Idea
Capability for divine assistance accompanies the act; capability for health and means precedes it.

Imam Maydani begins by clarifying a common confusion: there are two distinct meanings of 'capability' (istita'ah) in the Qur'an and Sunnah. One is the divine assistance that enables an action, which is present only at the moment of action. The other is the physical and mental capacity that is a prerequisite for the divine command. This lesson unpacks the first part of the passage where Maydani explains these two types and their relation to taklif.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types
Read the first sentences where Maydani distinguishes between the capability that is like tawfiq (cannot be attributed to creature) and the capability of health, means, and soundness. Notice the different timings: 'with the act' vs 'before the act'.
The verse 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity' supports the second type.
2
Understand the meaning of 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah'
Maydani explains this phrase as acknowledging that no one can avoid sin or perform obedience except with Allah's help. This illustrates the first type of capability (tawfiq).
3
Reflect on the relationship between the two types
Consider how the two types work together: the general capacity is present before, but the specific success (tawfiq) is granted at the time of action. This prevents the claim that humans are the ultimate creators of their actions.
This is key to the Ash'ari position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في أفعال العباد. والاستطاعة التي يجب بها الفعل من نحو التوفيق الذي لا يجوز أن يوصف المخلوق بها تكون مع الفعل، وأما الاستطاعة من الصحة والوسع والتمكن وسلامة الآلات فهي قبل الفعل وبها يتعلق الخطاب، وهو كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿لا يُكَلِّفُ اللهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا﴾. وأفعال العباد هي بخلق الله تعالى وكسب من العباد، ولم يكلفهم إلا ما يطيقونه ولا يطيقون إلا ما كلفهم، وهو حاصل تفسير قول: لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله تقول: لا حيلة ولا حركة لأحد عن معصية الله إلا بمعونة الله، ولا قوة لأحد على إقامة طاعة والثبات عليها إلا بتوفيق الله. والاستطاعة التي يجب أن يكون بها الفعل من نحو التوفيق الذي لا يجوز أن يوصف المخلوق بها وهي حقيقة القدرة تكون مع الفعل؛ قال صاحب التبصرة: إنها عرض يخلقه الله في الحيوان يفعل به الأفعال الاختيارية، وهي علة للفعل، والجمهور على أنها شرط لأداء الفعل لا علة. وبالجملة هي صفة يخلقها الله تعالى عند قصد اكتساب الفعل بعد سلامة الأسباب والآلات؛ فإن قصد فعل الخير خلق الله تعالى قدرة فعل الخير، وإن قصد فعل الشر خلق الله قدرة فعل الشر وكان هو المضيع القدرة فعل الخير فيستحق الذم والعقاب؛ ولهذا ذم الله تعالى الكافرين بأنهم لا يستطيعون السمع، وإذا كانت الاستطاعة عرضًا وجب أن تكون مقارنة للفعل بالزمان لا سابقة عليه وإلا لزم وقوع الفعل بلا استطاعة وقدرة عليه لما مر من امتناع بقاء
Speech on the actions of servants. The capability by which the act is obligatory, such as the divine assistance (tawfiq) which cannot be attributed to the created being, is with the act. As for the capability of health, capacity, ability, and soundness of limbs, it is before the act, and with it the command is connected, just as Allah Most High said: 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.' And the actions of servants are by Allah's creation and by acquisition (kasb) from the servants. He did not burden them except with what they are able to do, and they are not able except what He burdened them. This is the explanation of the saying: 'There is no might and no power except through Allah' — you say: There is no device and no movement for anyone to avoid disobedience to Allah except by Allah's assistance, and no power for anyone to perform obedience and remain steadfast upon it except by Allah's tawfiq. And the capability by which the act must be, of the type of tawfiq which cannot be attributed to the created being, and which is the reality of power (qudra), is with the act. The author of al-Tabsirah said: It is an accident (arad) that Allah creates in the living being by which he performs voluntary actions, and it is the cause of the act. But the majority hold that it is a condition for performing the act, not a cause. In summary, it is an attribute that Allah Most High creates at the time of intending to acquire the act, after soundness of causes and instruments. If he intends to do good, Allah creates the power to do good; if he intends to do evil, Allah creates the power to do evil, and it is he who wasted the power to do good, so he deserves blame and punishment. For this reason, Allah blamed the disbelievers that they cannot hear. And if capability is an accident, it must be simultaneous with the act in time, not preceding it, otherwise the act would occur without capability and power upon it, because of what has been mentioned regarding the impossibility of remaining
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a detailed theological discussion of the Ash'ari doctrine on human actions and capability (istita'ah). It begins by distinguishing two types of istita'ah: (1) the capability that accompanies the act, called tawfiq (divine assistance), which cannot be attributed to the creature; (2) the capability of health, capacity, and sound means, which precedes the act and is the basis for the divine command (taklif), as supported by the verse 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.' The passage then affirms that actions of servants are created by Allah and acquired (kasb) by the servant. The servant is only burdened with what he can do, and he can only do what he is burdened with. This is explained through the phrase 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah,' meaning no avoidance of sin or ability to obey except with Allah's help. Next, the passage examines the nature of the capability that accompanies the act. It quotes the author of al-Tabsirah who defines it as an accident (arad) created by Allah in the living being, enabling voluntary actions. There is a difference of opinion: some say it is a cause of the act, but the majority consider it a condition. In summary, it is an attribute created by Allah at the moment of intending to perform an act, after the soundness of causes and instruments. If one intends good, Allah creates the power for good; if evil, Allah creates the power for evil. However, the one who wastes the power for good is blameworthy, which is why Allah criticized the disbelievers for not being able to hear (i.e., they misuse their capability). Finally, it argues that if capability is an accident, it must be simultaneous with the act, not preceding it, otherwise the act would occur without capability, which is impossible.

Key Terms

التوفيق
القدرة
الكسب
الآلات
الخطاب
لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that capability is entirely within human control and that Allah's command is based on a capability that humans independently possess.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the capability that leads to actual performance (tawfiq) is from Allah and accompanies the act, while the capability of health and means is a prerequisite for the command but does not necessitate the act. Both forms of capability highlight human dependence on Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of capability is present with the act itself?
A) Capability of health and soundness
B) Capability of tawfiq (divine assistance)
C) Both types
D) Neither type

Key Takeaway
There are two types of capability: one is divine assistance that accompanies the act, and the other is general capacity that precedes it and is the basis of divine command.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah', do you truly believe that your ability to avoid sin comes entirely from Allah? Reflect on a moment you fell into sin despite knowing it was wrong — where was your reliance on Allah at that moment? What will you change today to make this du'a a reality in your struggles?
?
The passage distinguishes between the capability that precedes an action (your health, means, etc.) and the capability that accompanies the act (divine assistance). Think of an act of worship you are about to perform: are you relying more on your own preparedness or on Allah's tawfiq? How can you consciously invite Allah's tawfiq into that action?
?
Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity (general capability). Yet you might feel overwhelmed by some duties. Is that because you are confusing general capacity with the special tawfiq that comes at the moment of action? Confess to Allah where you have doubted His justice in what He has commanded you.

Divine Creation of Actions and the Nature of Kasb
Maydani discusses the detailed nature of capability as an accident, the difference between cause and condition, and the theological proof for simultaneity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position that Allah creates both the action and the ability, while humans acquire (kasb) the action and that the ability is an accident created simultaneously with the act.

Core Idea
Allah creates the act and the power; the servant acquires and is responsible.

In the previous lesson, we learned about two types of capability. Now Maydani delves deeper into the nature of the capability that accompanies the act and its relationship to the act itself. He explains that this capability is an accident (arad) created by Allah in the living being, and there is a scholarly difference on whether it is a cause or a condition of the act. He also addresses the timing: this capability must be simultaneous with the act, not preceding it, otherwise the act would occur without it. This lesson unpacks the second part of the passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the nature of capability
Maydani quotes the author of al-Tabsirah who defines the capability (qudra) as an accident created by Allah in the living being, enabling voluntary actions. Note the two views: cause vs condition.
The majority view is that it is a condition, not a cause.
2
Understand the creation of power at the moment of intention
Allah creates the specific power for good or evil based on the servant's intention after the soundness of causes and instruments. The servant who intends evil wastes the power for good and is blameworthy.
3
Comprehend the argument for simultaneity
If capability is an accident, it cannot endure and must exist at the same time as the act. Otherwise, the act would occur without capability, which is impossible.
This defends the doctrine that all power is from Allah at every moment.

الكلام في أفعال العباد. والاستطاعة التي يجب بها الفعل من نحو التوفيق الذي لا يجوز أن يوصف المخلوق بها تكون مع الفعل، وأما الاستطاعة من الصحة والوسع والتمكن وسلامة الآلات فهي قبل الفعل وبها يتعلق الخطاب، وهو كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿لا يُكَلِّفُ اللهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا﴾. وأفعال العباد هي بخلق الله تعالى وكسب من العباد، ولم يكلفهم إلا ما يطيقونه ولا يطيقون إلا ما كلفهم، وهو حاصل تفسير قول: لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله تقول: لا حيلة ولا حركة لأحد عن معصية الله إلا بمعونة الله، ولا قوة لأحد على إقامة طاعة والثبات عليها إلا بتوفيق الله. والاستطاعة التي يجب أن يكون بها الفعل من نحو التوفيق الذي لا يجوز أن يوصف المخلوق بها وهي حقيقة القدرة تكون مع الفعل؛ قال صاحب التبصرة: إنها عرض يخلقه الله في الحيوان يفعل به الأفعال الاختيارية، وهي علة للفعل، والجمهور على أنها شرط لأداء الفعل لا علة. وبالجملة هي صفة يخلقها الله تعالى عند قصد اكتساب الفعل بعد سلامة الأسباب والآلات؛ فإن قصد فعل الخير خلق الله تعالى قدرة فعل الخير، وإن قصد فعل الشر خلق الله قدرة فعل الشر وكان هو المضيع القدرة فعل الخير فيستحق الذم والعقاب؛ ولهذا ذم الله تعالى الكافرين بأنهم لا يستطيعون السمع، وإذا كانت الاستطاعة عرضًا وجب أن تكون مقارنة للفعل بالزمان لا سابقة عليه وإلا لزم وقوع الفعل بلا استطاعة وقدرة عليه لما مر من امتناع بقاء
Speech on the actions of servants. The capability by which the act is obligatory, such as the divine assistance (tawfiq) which cannot be attributed to the created being, is with the act. As for the capability of health, capacity, ability, and soundness of limbs, it is before the act, and with it the command is connected, just as Allah Most High said: 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.' And the actions of servants are by Allah's creation and by acquisition (kasb) from the servants. He did not burden them except with what they are able to do, and they are not able except what He burdened them. This is the explanation of the saying: 'There is no might and no power except through Allah' — you say: There is no device and no movement for anyone to avoid disobedience to Allah except by Allah's assistance, and no power for anyone to perform obedience and remain steadfast upon it except by Allah's tawfiq. And the capability by which the act must be, of the type of tawfiq which cannot be attributed to the created being, and which is the reality of power (qudra), is with the act. The author of al-Tabsirah said: It is an accident (arad) that Allah creates in the living being by which he performs voluntary actions, and it is the cause of the act. But the majority hold that it is a condition for performing the act, not a cause. In summary, it is an attribute that Allah Most High creates at the time of intending to acquire the act, after soundness of causes and instruments. If he intends to do good, Allah creates the power to do good; if he intends to do evil, Allah creates the power to do evil, and it is he who wasted the power to do good, so he deserves blame and punishment. For this reason, Allah blamed the disbelievers that they cannot hear. And if capability is an accident, it must be simultaneous with the act in time, not preceding it, otherwise the act would occur without capability and power upon it, because of what has been mentioned regarding the impossibility of remaining

The Middle Path on Human Actions
States the Ash'ari middle path on human actions, refuting Jabriyya and Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari doctrine of human actions, how it avoids the extremes of Jabriyya and Qadariyya, and the key distinction between divine creation (khalq) and human acquisition (kasb).

Core Idea
Human actions are created by Allah and acquired by the servant.

This passage presents the Sunni position on human actions, one of the most debated topics in Islamic theology. It carefully navigates between two extreme views: one that denies human responsibility and another that denies divine power. By reading this text, you will see how the Ash'ari school affirms both divine predestination and human accountability through the concept of kasb (acquisition).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Get a feel for the author's concise style.
Notice the key terms 'khalq' and 'kasb' appear early.
2
Identify the two extreme sects
Find the refutations of Jabriyya and Qadariyya. What does each group believe? How does the author describe them?
Jabriyya are compared to a person with tremors; Qadariyya claim independence from Allah.
3
Understand the middle path
The Ahl al-Sunna take the middle path: actions are by Allah's creation and the servant's acquisition. Look for the Qur'anic proof (2:286).
The verse uses both 'kasaba' and 'iktasaba' to attribute actions to the soul.
4
Grasp the distinction between khalq and kasb
The author explains that a single action can be attributed to Allah as creation and to the servant as acquisition, from two different aspects. This resolves the apparent contradiction.
There is no impossibility in one thing falling under two powers from two different aspects.
5
Reflect on the implications
Think about how this doctrine preserves both divine omnipotence and human moral responsibility. Why is this important for Islamic theology?
This answers the common misunderstanding that predestination negates free will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَفْعَالُ العِبَادِ هِيَ بِخَلْقِ الله تَعَالَى وَكَسْبٍ مِنَ العِبَادِ، وَلَمْ يُكَلِّفُهُمْ إِلَّا مَا يُطِيقُونَهُ وَلَا يُطِيقُونَ إِلَّا مَا كَلَّفَهُمْ، وَهُوَ حَاصِلُ تَفْسِيرِ قَوْلِ: لَا حَوْلَ وَلَا قُوَّةَ إِلَّا بِالله. وَأَفْعَالُ جَمِيعِ العِبَادِ إِنَّهَا هِيَ بِخَلْقِ الله تَعَالَى وَكَسْبٍ مِنَ العِبَادِ خِلَافًا لِلْجَبْرِيَّةِ الْقَائِلِينَ بِأَنَّهَا مِنَ الله تَعَالَى خَلْقًا وَإِيجَادًا وَلَمْ يُثْبِتُوا لِلْعِبَادِ قُدْرَةً بَلْ جَعَلُوهَا كُلَّهَا اضْطِرَارِيَّةً كَحَرَكَاتِ المُرْتَعِشِ، وَلِلْقَدَرِيَّةِ الْقَائِلِينَ بِأَنَّهَا مِنَ العَبْدِ خَلْقًا وَإِيجَادًا دُونَ رَبِّهِمْ، وَأَثْبَتُوا لِأَنْفُسِهِمْ غِنًى عَنِ اللهِ، وَتَوَسَّطَتْ أَهْلُ السُّنَّةِ بِأَنَّهَا بِخَلْقِ الله وَكَسْبِ العَبْدِ بِدَلِيلِ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿لَهَا مَا كَسَبَتْ وَعَلَيْهَا مَا اكْتَسَبَتْ﴾ [سورة البقرة آية: ٢٨٦]. وَالفَرْقُ بَيْنَ الخَلْقِ وَالكَسْبِ أَنَّ المَقْدُورَ مُخْتَرَعٌ وَمُكْتَسَبٌ؛ فَمِنْ حَيْثُ كَوْنُهُ مَخْلُوقًا يُضَافُ إِلَى الله تَعَالَى بِجِهَةِ الاخْتِرَاعِ، وَمِنْ حَيْثُ كَوْنُهُ كَسْبًا يُضَافُ إِلَى العَبْدِ، وَلَا اسْتِحَالَةَ فِي دُخُولِ مَقْدُورٍ وَاحِدٍ تَحْتَ قُدْرَةِ قَادِرَيْنِ بِجِهَتَيْنِ مُخْتَلِفَتَيْنِ إِحْدَاهُمَا خَلْقًا، وَهِيَ خَارِجَةٌ عَنْ مَقْدُورِ العَبْدِ، وَالأُخْرَى كَسْبًا لِلْعَبْدِ بِإِقْدَارِ الله تَعَالَى.
And the actions of the servants are by the creation (khalq) of Allah Most High and acquisition (kasb) from the servants. And He did not obligate them except what they can do, and they cannot do except what He obligated them. And that is the conclusion of the interpretation of the saying: 'There is no power and no strength except by Allah.' And the actions of all the servants are by the creation of Allah Most High and acquisition from the servants, contrary to the Jabriyya who say that they are from Allah Most High by creation and origination, and they did not affirm for the servants any power, but rather made them all compelled like the movements of a tremor sufferer; and contrary to the Qadariyya who say that they are from the servant by creation and origination without their Lord, and they affirmed for themselves independence from Allah. And the Ahl al-Sunna took the middle path: they are by the creation of Allah and the acquisition of the servant, as evidence of His statement Most High: 'For it is what it has earned, and against it is what it has acquired' (Sūrat al-Baqara, 2:286). And the difference between creation (khalq) and acquisition (kasb) is that the thing brought into existence (al-maqdūr) is both invented (mukhtaraʿ) and acquired (muktasab). Insofar as it is created, it is attributed to Allah Most High by the aspect of invention (ikhtirāʿ); and insofar as it is acquisition, it is attributed to the servant. And there is no impossibility in one thing brought into existence falling under the power of two powerful beings from two different aspects: one of them is creation, which is outside the power of the servant, and the other is acquisition for the servant by the enabling (iqdār) of Allah Most High.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage presents the Ashʿarī doctrine on human actions, known as the middle path between Jabriyya (absolute compulsion) and Qadariyya (absolute self-determination). The author begins by affirming that actions of servants are by Allah's creation (khalq) and the servant's acquisition (kasb). This is derived from the meaning of the phrase 'lā ḥawla wa lā quwwata illā billāh' (there is no power and no strength except by Allah). He then explicitly refutes two extremist sects: the Jabriyya, who claim actions are purely from Allah with no human power, likening humans to a person with involuntary tremors; and the Qadariyya, who claim actions are purely from the servant, independent of Allah. The Ahl al-Sunna (Sunni Muslims) take the middle path, proving it with Qurʾān 2:286, which attributes both 'earned' (kasaba) and 'acquired' (iktasaba) to the human soul. Then the author explains the distinction between khalq and kasb: a single action can be considered under two aspects—as created (mukhtaraʿ) it is attributed to Allah because He is the creator; as acquired (muktasab) it is attributed to the servant because the servant performs it with the power created by Allah. There is no contradiction in one thing falling under two powers from different aspects: Allah's power creates the action, and the servant's power (which is also created) acquires it. The servant's power is not independent but is enabled (iqdār) by Allah. This resolves the problem of divine predestination and human responsibility.

Key Terms
الخلق
الكسب
الجبرية
القدرية
الاختراع
الاقتدار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If Allah creates all actions, then humans are compelled and have no free will.
Correction: The Ash'ari distinction: Allah creates the action as an invention (ikhtirāʿ), but the servant acquires it (kasb) by performing it with a power created by Allah, thus preserving human responsibility.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the difference between creation (khalq) and acquisition (kasb) regarding human actions?
A) Creation is by Allah, acquisition is by the servant.
B) Creation is by the servant, acquisition is by Allah.
C) Both are by Allah.
D) Both are by the servant.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari solution harmonizes divine sovereignty and human accountability by distinguishing between Allah's creation of actions and the servant's acquisition of them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every action you take—from your heartbeat to your decision to pray or sin—is created by Allah? How does this belief affect your sense of dependence on Him in your daily life?
?
When you commit a major sin, do you tend to blame yourself completely (as if you created the sin independently) or feel that Allah created it and therefore you are not responsible? How does the Ash'ari distinction between creation and acquisition lead you to a more balanced response?
?
If you are in a state where you feel weak and unable to do good, how does the phrase 'lā ḥawla wa lā quwwata illā billāh' become a practical weapon in your life? What specific step will you take today to rely on Allah's power for a task you have been avoiding?

Resolving the Objection: Two Meanings of Power
Imam Maydani refutes the objection that capacity must be before the act by distinguishing two meanings of power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the objection that capacity must be before the act fails, and how the distinction between two meanings of power resolves it.

Core Idea
Power is twofold: real power with the act, and capacity before the act — obligations attach to the latter.

This passage presents a common objection against the Ash'ari position that power (qudra) is simultaneous with the act. Objectors argue that since obligations exist before the act, capacity must also exist before it, otherwise we would be commanding the incapable. Imam Maydani answers by distinguishing two meanings of 'power' and supports this with Quranic verses. This lesson walks through the objection, the response, and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Understand the argument that capacity must be before the act because obligations are before it; otherwise, it would be imposing on the incapable.
The objectors use the examples of the disbeliever's obligation to believe and the prayer abandoner's obligation after time enters.
2
Identify the two meanings
Note the author's distinction: real power (haqiqat al-qudra) is with the act, while capacity as health, scope, and soundness of means is before the act.
Obligations are attached to this second meaning.
3
See the Quranic proof
Reflect on how verses 2:286 and 3:97 use capacity in the sense of health and means, supporting the author's distinction.
These verses show that capacity is understood before the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما استدل القائلون بكون الاستطاعة قبل الفعل بأن التكاليف قبل الفعل؛ ضرورة أن الكافر مكلف بالإيمان وتارك الصلاة مكلف بها بعد دخول الوقت فلو لم تكن الاستطاعة محققة حينئذ لزم تكليف العاجز وهو باطل - أشار إلى الجواب بقوله: (وأما الاستطاعة من الصحة والوسع والتمكن من الفعل وسلامة الآلات والأسباب فهي قبل الفعل) والحاصل أن القدرة لها إطلاقان؛ فتطلق تارة ويراد بها حقيقة القدرة وهي مع الفعل، وتطلق أخرى ويراد بها الوسع والسلامة وهي قبل الفعل، (وبها) أي الاستطاعة بالمعنى الثاني يتعلق الخطاب والتكليف (وهو كما قال الله تعالى لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا) [سورة البقرة آية : ٢٨٦] وقوله : (وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حجُ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِيلًا ) (سورة آل عمران آية: ٩٧].
When those who argue that capacity (istita'ah) is before the act adduced as evidence that obligations are before the act—necessarily because the disbeliever is obliged to believe and the one who abandons prayer is obliged to perform it after the time enters, so if capacity were not actual at that time, it would necessitate imposing upon the incapable, which is false—[the author] pointed to the answer by saying: 'As for capacity in the sense of health, scope, ability to perform, and soundness of limbs and means, it is before the act.' The summary is that power (qudra) has two usages: sometimes it is used meaning the reality of power, and that is with the act; and sometimes it is used meaning scope and soundness, and that is before the act. And by it (i.e., capacity in the second sense) the address and obligation are attached. And it is as Allah said: 'Allah does not burden a soul except with its capacity' [Surah al-Baqarah 2:286] and His saying: 'And Allah has upon people the pilgrimage to the House for whoever is able to find a way to it' [Surah Aal-e-Imran 3:97].
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. The objectors argue that capacity must be before the act because obligations are before the act: e.g., a disbeliever is obliged to believe at the time of the call, and the one who abandons prayer is obliged after time enters. If capacity (the ability to perform) were not present at that time, it would be imposing a duty on the incapable, which is invalid. The author answers by distinguishing two meanings of power (qudra). The first is 'real power' which is the ability to create an effect; that exists only with the act itself. The second is 'capacity' in the sense of health, scope, soundness of organs, and means; this exists before the act. It is this second meaning to which obligations are attached. The author supports this with two Quranic verses: 'Allah does not burden a soul except with its capacity' (2:286) and the Hajj verse (3:97), which clearly speak of capacity before the act. Thus the objection fails because the obligation is based on the second meaning, not the first.

Key Terms
الاستطاعة (istita'ah)
القدرة (qudra)
الوسع (wus')
التكليف (taklif)
حقيقة القدرة (haqiqat al-qudra)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Capacity must exist before the act in the same sense as the ability to create an effect (real power).
Correction: Capacity has two senses: real power is with the act, but capacity as health and means is before the act. Obligations are attached to the latter.

Checkpoint
What is the objection addressed in this passage?
A) Capacity must be with the act, otherwise it is impossible.
B) Capacity must be before the act because obligations are before the act, otherwise it would be imposing on the incapable.
C) Capacity is created by Allah and acquired by the servant.
D) There is no such thing as capacity before the act.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between real power (with the act) and capacity (before the act) resolves the objection that obligations require capacity before the act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used the excuse 'I don't have the ability' to avoid an obligation that Allah has placed upon you, even though you had the means? How does the distinction between real power and capacity challenge that excuse?
?
When you read the verse 'Allah does not burden a soul except with its capacity', do you truly believe that every command Allah gives you is within your capability, or do you sometimes feel overwhelmed? What might that reveal about your understanding of your own capacity?
?
The objectors in the passage were concerned about justice. But are you more concerned about your own comfort than about fulfilling obligations? Reflect on an obligatory act you delay because you think you lack the power now — how does this lesson call you to respond?

The Middle Path: Divine Creation and Human Acquisition
Imam Maydani presents the views of Jabriyya, Qadariyya, and Ahl al-Sunna on human acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on human acts (kasb) and how it differs from Jabriyya and Qadariyya.

Core Idea
Allah creates the act; the servant acquires it.

This lesson introduces a crucial theological debate about human responsibility. Imam Maydani presents three competing views, showing how Ahl al-Sunna steers a middle course between fatalism and self-sufficiency.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the three schools are introduced in quick succession.
2
Contrast the three schools
Identify the positions of Jabriyya, Qadariyya, and Ahl al-Sunna. How do they differ on the origin of human acts? Write a short comparison.
3
Reflect on the proof
Examine the Quranic verse cited (2:286). How does it support the Sunni middle path? Try to explain the concept of kasb in your own words.
Kasb means acquisition, not creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأفعال جميع العباد إنها يخلق الله تعالى وكسب من العباد خلافًا للجبرية القائلين بأنها من الله تعالى خلقا وإيجادا ولم يثبتوا للعباد قدرة بل جعلوها كلها اضطرارية كحركات المرتعش وللقدرية القائلين بأنها من العبد خلقا وإيجادا دون ربهم، وأثبتوا لأنفسهم غنى عن الله، وتوسطت أهل السنة بأنها بخلق الله وكسب العبد بدليل قوله تعالى: (لَهَا مَا كَسَبَتْ وَعَلَهَا مَا اكْتَسَبَتْ) [سورة البقرة آية: ٢٨٦].
And the acts of all servants are created by Allah, may He be exalted, and acquired (kasb) by the servants, contrary to the Jabriyya who say that they are from Allah, may He be exalted, by creation and origination, and did not affirm any power for the servants, but rather made them all involuntary like the movements of a person with tremors, and contrary to the Qadariyya who say that they are from the servant by creation and origination without their Lord, and they affirmed for themselves independence from Allah. And Ahl al-Sunna took the middle path: that they are by the creation of Allah and the acquisition of the servant, as evidence by His saying: 'For it (the soul) is what it has earned, and against it is what it has acquired' [Surah al-Baqarah 2:286].
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage classifies three theological schools on human acts. (1) The Jabriyya (fatalists) hold that all human acts are purely created by Allah, with no real power in the servant; they are entirely involuntary, like the tremors of a sick person. (2) The Qadariyya (free-willers) hold that the servant creates his own acts independently of Allah, asserting self-sufficiency. (3) Ahl al-Sunna (the Sunnis) take the middle path: acts are created by Allah in terms of origination (khalq), but acquired (kasb) by the servant in terms of responsibility. The proof is the Quranic verse (2:286) which attributes earning (kasb and iktisab) to the soul, showing that while Allah is the Creator, the servant has a role of acquisition.

Key Terms
الجبرية (al-Jabriyya)
القدرية (al-Qadariyya)
أهل السنة (Ahl al-Sunna)
الخلق (khalq)
الكسب (kasb)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Kasb means the servant creates his own act.
Correction: Kasb means acquisition, not creation. The servant earns the act by performing it, but its existence is from Allah.

Checkpoint
According to Ahl al-Sunna, human acts are...
A) Created solely by Allah with no role for the servant.
B) Created solely by the servant independently.
C) Created by Allah and acquired by the servant.
D) Both created by Allah and the servant together.

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunna affirms both divine creation and human responsibility through the concept of kasb, avoiding fatalism and self-sufficiency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking, 'It was Allah's will; I had no choice'? How does the Sunni teaching on kasb strip away that excuse and place responsibility back on you?
?
Think of a good deed you did today. In that moment, did you feel pride thinking you alone created it? How does acknowledging Allah as the Creator of that act change your heart—does it humble you or push you to thank Him more?
?
If every action you perform is simultaneously created by Allah and acquired by you, what does that mean for your daily struggle against sin? Will you rely more on Allah's help or on your own strength? Answer honestly.

The Difference Between Creation and Acquisition
Imam Maydani explains khalq vs kasb and two movements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key distinction between khalq (creation) and kasb (acquisition), and why a single act can be attributed to both Allah and the servant without contradiction.

Core Idea
Creation is Allah’s invention; acquisition is the servant’s derived capacity.

This passage clarifies a central doctrine in Islamic theology regarding human action. How can an act be both created by Allah and acquired by the servant? Imam Maydani resolves this by distinguishing the aspects of attribution, then illustrates with two types of movement to show what is subject to obligation.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the core distinction
Read the opening sentence: the brought-into-existence is both invented and acquired. Understand that 'creation' is Allah's aspect, 'acquisition' is the servant's.
Note the key terms: khalq and kasb.
2
Understand the two-aspect attribution
See how one act can be under two powers without contradiction—each aspect is different. Creation is Allah's exclusive power; acquisition is the servant's by Allah's enabling.
This resolves the theological puzzle of divine predestination and human responsibility.
3
Apply to the two types of movement
Read about involuntary movement (no obligation) and voluntary movement (obligation applies). Recognize that only voluntary acts are subject to command and prohibition.
Involuntary acts like trembling are purely Allah's creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والفرق بين الخلق والكسب أن المقدور مخترع ومكتسب؛ فمن حيث كونه مخلوقا يضاف إلى الله تعالى بجهة الاختراع، ومن حيث كونه كسبا يضاف إلى العبد، ولا استحالة في دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قادرين بجهتين مختلفتين إحداهما خلقا، وهي خارجة عن مقدور العبد، والأخرى كسبا للعبد بإقدار الله تعالى، ثم إن الباري تعالى تارة يخلق في العبد حركة جبرية لا يقدر على الامتناع عنها كحركة المرتعش؛ فهذه محض مقدور الله تعالى خلقا وإيجادا، وتارة حركة اختيارية عند قصد العبد ويقدره على صرفها إلى أي فعل شاء إلا أن الله يأمره بصرفها إلى الطاعة وينهاه عن صرفها إلى المعاصي؛ فكان تكليفا بما للعبد قدرة على الإيتاء به والامتناع عنه؛ ولهذا في الحركة الجبرية لم يرد الأمر بها والنهي عنها ولم يتعلق بها تكليف.
And the difference between creation and acquisition is that the brought-into-existence (maqdur) is invented (mukhtara') and acquired (muktasab). So from the aspect of its being created, it is attributed to Allah, may He be exalted, in the manner of invention; and from the aspect of its being an acquisition, it is attributed to the servant. And there is no impossibility in a single brought-into-existence falling under the power of two powerful agents from two different aspects: one being creation, which is beyond the power of the servant, and the other being acquisition for the servant by Allah's enabling him. Then, the Exalted Creator sometimes creates in the servant an involuntary movement that he cannot refrain from, like the movement of a tremulous person; this is purely the power of Allah, may He be exalted, by creation and origination. And sometimes (He creates) a voluntary movement when the servant intends it and empowers him to direct it to whichever action he wishes, except that Allah commands him to direct it to obedience and forbids him from directing it to sins. Thus obligation is attached to that which the servant has power to bring about and refrain from. Hence, in the case of involuntary movement, there is no command or prohibition, and no obligation is attached to it.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the key terms khalq (creation) and kasb (acquisition). It begins by stating that a single act can be both 'created' (mukhtara') and 'acquired' (muktasab). From the aspect of its being created, it is attributed to Allah as the Inventor; from the aspect of its being acquired, it is attributed to the servant. There is no contradiction in one act being under two powers if the aspects differ: one is real creative power (Allah's), the other is a derived enabling power (the servant's). The author then illustrates with two types of movement: (1) Involuntary movement (e.g., trembling), which is purely Allah's creation and the servant has no effective power over it; (2) Voluntary movement, where Allah creates the movement when the servant intends it and gives him the capacity to direct it. It is this voluntary movement that is subject to obligation—command and prohibition. Involuntary movement carries no obligation. This clarifies that the servant's acquisition is real but not independent; it is derived from Allah's enabling.

Key Terms
الخلق
الكسب
المقدور
الحركة الجبرية
الحركة الاختيارية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is impossible for one act to be attributed to both Allah and the servant.
Correction: It is possible from different aspects: creation (invention) by Allah and acquisition by the servant; the two attributions do not conflict.

Checkpoint
What is the difference between creation and acquisition according to this passage?
A) Creation is purely from the servant, acquisition from Allah.
B) Creation is attribution by invention (to Allah), acquisition is attribution to the servant.
C) They are the same.
D) Creation is involuntary, acquisition is voluntary.

Key Takeaway
A single act can be both created by Allah (by invention) and acquired by the servant (by enabling), and only voluntary actions carry obligation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time you blamed your own sin on circumstances or said 'I couldn't help it.' Does this lesson expose that as a false excuse? How will you now take full responsibility for your voluntary sins?
?
This lesson says involuntary movements have no obligation. But what about your inward intentions and desires? Are they involuntary? How do you distinguish between temptations you cannot control and choices you can? What does this mean for your accountability before Allah?
?
Allah commands you to direct your voluntary actions to obedience. In what area of your life are you pretending your disobedience is involuntary? What will you do today to reclaim your agency and obey?
